CSP-O
Chinese Syndicalist Party - Orthodox (Zhongguo Gongtuandang - Zhengtong Pai)\n§LSlightly deviating from the more urban, industrial and union-based syndicalism of the CSP mainstream, the CSP in Sichuan primarily springs from the group of Sichuanese intelligentsia that went abroad to France for work-study programs in the Great War, led by Wu Yuzhang among others.\n\nConnected with the various Sino-French education initiatives and spending time in France during both the war as well as the ensuing revolution, Wu Yuzhang and his fellow intellectuals would arrive back in China to capitalise on the waves of revolutionary fervour that followed the end of the Weltkrieg. Inspired by socialist thought but disheartened by the lack of unity within the Chinese revolution, which had fractured into revolutionary and reformist camps, Wu would spend the 1920s reading the works of socialist thinkers like John Reed, concluding the need for a clear ideological agenda, one which he found within the CSP. This agenda would be expanded with Wu's manifesto of the Sichuan Autonomous Federation, advocating for not only a transformation of the social economy and mutual assistance programs for workers, but an end to \
East Sichuan Red Army
Eastern Sichuan Red Army Guerrilla Force (Chuandong Hongjun Youjidui)\n§LThroughout the warlord era, Sichuan, much like its Southern neighbours, has been a hotbed for socialist guerrillas and intellectual activity, though this has been counterbalanced heavily by militarist repression and gentry influence. A keystone in China's agricultural heartland, Sichuan's agrarian nature has resulted in the Red Basin providing a fertile base of support that is sympathetic to the socialist cause.\n\nDuring the Northern Expedition, many members from both the LKMT and the CSP, some of whom had trained as junior officers at Whampoa, conducted irregular activities to disrupt the movements of warlord forces. One of the main actions was the failed Lushun uprising led by Liu Bocheng, Zhu De and Yang Angong in late 1926, which aimed to revolt in tandem with a renewed NRA push and disrupt warlord supply in the Sichuanese backwater. Though unsuccessful, the Lushun uprising would fan the revolutionary flames of the peasantry, refine the strategy of future guerrilla warfare and inspire others like Li Jiajun and Wang Weizhou to also conduct armed resistance in the countryside, resulting in the surprisingly successful Gujunba uprising in 1929.\n\nThe tumults of the 1930s have seen the peasant insurgencies primarily in Eastern Sichuan slowly being pushed back as consolidating militarists like Liao Zhen aim to wipe them out wholesale. Despite this, resistance has been resolute, with many more guerrilla cells mobilising to take the place of the fallen. These militias and revolutionaries have been reorganised in recent years into the East Sichuan Red Army Guerrilla Force, led by a committee headed by Wang Weizhou and split into three route armies, its strength bolstered by more irregular formations like the Fuling Peasant Army and CSP insurgent cells. But for all these developments, it remains to be seen if the last holdouts of both the KMT's agrarian bloc and the CSP in Sichuan have what it takes to wrestle control of the divided province when the time comes.§!\n

Officer Department
$SZC_social_liberal_party_long_tt$\n§LUnlike the other departments, which all derive their namesake from key military academies, the Officer Department would develop from the graduates of the fourth and fifth classes of the Sichuan Preliminary Army School that had also been created under the Qing administration. These officers would become a key component under Baoding leadership, with both Li Jiayu and Luo Zezhou commanding their forces under Deng Xihou until their split with him in late 1929.\n\nIn 1927, Li and Luo would be stationed as divisional commanders around Suining, opting to form the Qunyi Society, a loose organisation aiming to attract new graduates from the Sichuan Army Officer School. The collapse of the Sichuan Frontier Defence Army and the forced resignation of its commander Liu Chengxun during the Central Sichuan War also brought one of his subordinates, Lai Xinhui, into the Officer Department, bolstering their numbers.\n\nHesitant to throw their lot in with any one of their significantly stronger opponents, the Officers have largely succeeded in staying neutral to both the Liu brothers as well as the Zhili provincial leaders throughout the early 1930s. Uniquely, however, the lower-ranking commanders of this department are remarkably progressive, with these ideals even championed by Li Jiayu himself, allowing for the Officer Department to be receptive to elements of federalism, democracy and even some aspects of the KMT.§!\n
Industrial Corps
Industrial Corps (Shiye Tuan)\n§LWith their foundation in the non-military sector, the Industrial Corps would primarily be comprised of graduates from the Sichuan Higher Education Academy, aligned with the centre and right of the KMT. Possessing no real central leader owing to the group's hybrid civilian and military wings, the Industrial Corps would begin as subordinates in Xiong Kewu's campaigns against Yuan Shikai and other warlords in the late 1910s. Though initially allied, Xiong's dissatisfaction with Sun Yat-sen's appointment of Yang Shukan as Sichuanese governor in 1918 as well as the removal of Industrial Corps figures from the army by Xiong would result in the Industrial Corps taking their chance during the Yunnanese invasion of 1920 to rebel against him, resulting in the corps' expulsion from the province.\n\nIndustrial Corps activity in Sichuan would not pick up again until Lü Chao's return to the province in June 1923 under orders by Sun Yat-sen. After playing the provincial strongmen of Liu Xiang, Yang Sen and even Yuan Zuming against each other, Lü Chao would find himself with a small defence zone and army, attempting to rally his subordinates to the KMT cause prior to the abortive Northern Expedition. After the collapse of the Guangzhou government, Lü found himself isolated once more, trapped along the Yunnan-Sichuan border and with hostile external forces waiting for an opportune moment to pounce.\n\nThis chance would arise as the 1930s dawned and encirclement campaigns into the mountains began. Hemmed in by Liu Wenhui's men to the West, Pan Wenhua's Southern Bandit Suppression Command to the North and East as well as Long Yun's Zhaotong Defence Commission to the South, Lü Chao had no choice but to melt further into the countryside, where his battered force try to make contact with the main RKMT junta in Guizhou. Even though they are considered a spent force for now, any form of catastrophic instability could prove to be the second wind Lü so desperately needs.§!\n

Armament Department
Armament Department (Wubei xi)\n§LOriginating from the late Qing Sichuanese rearmament movement, the Armament Department remains the oldest of the cliques within Sichuan, comprised of predominantly senior military figures who graduated from the Sichuan Armament Academy established in 1902. Upon the takeover of the inland province by Hu Jingyi and Yin Changheng in 1911, the Armament Department influence would only increase, with all echelons of Sichuan command being staffed with Armament graduates and alumni. During the reign of Yuan Shikai, the Armament Department would split into Hu Jingyi's loyalist faction and Liu Cunhou's Sichuanese National Protection Army. However, with Hu being moved to Beijing, and his successor Chen Huan declaring the province's independence, the new de jure governor Luo Peijin held little sway in provincial affairs, resulting in his ousting by Liu Cunhou.\n\nLiu remained at the head of the Armament Department through the intervening years, leading campaigns against extra-provincial forces from Yunnan and Guizhou, Xiong Kewu's army and bandits, while also taking various sides in Sichuan's decades of militarist squabbles, being swept in and out of power all throughout. He would ultimately be appointed by the Zhili as head of the Sichuan-Shaanxi Border Defence Supervisory Office in 1924, obtaining jurisdiction in Sichuan's North-east.\n\n\

CDL-NCRA
$SZC_CDL_ncra_long_tt$\n§L$GXC_CDL_intro$\n\nA growing political force attached to a titan of Sichuanese politics, the New Century Research Association, founded by leftist Zhou Taixuan and now headed by Zhang Lan, has been a rallying point for all progressives, new federalists and socialists alike. Coalescing informally from Zhang Lan's closest associates in his governing of Nanchong county in the early 1920s and his leadership in the Sichuan Rural Construction Association in 1927, the NCRA is the latest rendition of Zhang's political coalition as China's reunification draws near.\n\nBased on the Provisional Autonomy Charter of Nanchong County and Zhang's early years cooperating with republicans of all persuasions, the NCRA's policies centre around one of industrial autonomy and the reorientation of education to attain it, though many remain wary of the increasing leftist tilt of Zhang's new political apparatus.§!\n

PFAPO
$SZC_Provincial_Federal_Autonomy_party_long_tt$\n§LHaving been confined to Hunan-administered Guizhou for nearly a decade, Xiong Kewu and his Nine-Man Regiment have been handed a mandate once more, not only on the battlefield but by the people of Sichuan who yearn for change.\n\nConsolidating and organising for more formal governance, Xiong has formed the Provincial Federal Autonomy Preparatory Office to begin addressing the province's concerns and complaints after the recent cessation and stabilisation of by far the most fractured province in China. The PFAPO has been effective thus far in inducting new intellect into its ranks and its members have been active in communicating the goals of federalism to the masses. In terms of administrative style, though, Xiong and his men have also taken partially from what they have observed from Zhao Hengti's Hunanese Assembly during their short stints there in both 1924 and again in 1928, ingratiating themselves with the local conservative gentry and business interests while simultaneously being careful not to alienate the farmers and workers that make up most of Sichuan.\n\nRegardless, the PFAPO remains vigilant against Sichuan's main threats of banditry, resource scarcity and the persistent scheming of petty warlords, which are all frequent sources of social discontent that threaten to tarnish Xiong's standing with the public.§!\n
Provincial Federal Autonomy Preparation Office (Liansheng Zizhi Choubei Chu)
PWS
$SZC_Public_Welfare_Society_long_tt$\n§LBased around Dayi County, the Public Welfare Society, headed by Liu Wenhui's brother Liu Wencai, has become quite a controversial institution. Ostensibly formed as a philanthropist and charity organisation, the PWS has instead become infamous across Sichuan as a front for the vast provincial patronage networks, brotherhood secret societies, various bandit leaders and scheming rural landlords. Liu Wencai himself has become notorious as the main perpetrator of some of the society's worst excesses, not only being a ruthless landlord, but also extorting and taxing civilians for everything from prostitution to owning farming implements.\n\nCivil authorities across Sichuan, particularly those on the frontier, have found themselves frequently strong-armed by members of the PWS and the militia attached to the organ. Local courts and taxation offices have been exploited purely for the means of enriching Liu Wencai and his cronies. Liu's connections with the remnants of the provincial Chamber of Commerce have also worsened the influence of the PWS, with the few merchants who used their wits and financial resources to reach secret deals with local warlords now also falling under Liu Wencai's authority.\n\nLiu Wenhui's attempts to keep his brother in check up to this point have been ineffective, with the PWS and its connections in the Pao-Ge - the Sichuanese Gelaohui still eclipsing formal administrative posts in controlling economic and neighbourhood activity.§!\n
Public Welfare Society (Gongyi Xie Jin She)
GRA-UFAA
$SZC_gra_ufaa_long_tt$\n§L$GXC_GRA_intro$\n\nWith roots from the early movements and societies of the 20s and 30s whereby various Sichuanese intellectuals experimented with Federal Autonomy, the United Federal Autonomy Association is the natural successor to such constitutionalist groups. Like many of its extra-provincial electoral allies in the Grand Republican Alliance, the UFAA champions the drafting of provincial constitutions, reorganising civil administration and a broad demobilisation of the national army upon the conclusion of most of the fighting that had plagued China.\n\nHeaded by Xiong's long-time ally following the Long-gowned General's step back from electoral politics, Dan Maoxin has continued to promote the Federalist cause, with the UFAA differing from their opponents by being more willing to compromise and enter into alliances with other republican factions like Beiyang Independents or remnants of the Political Science Clique. Despite slight differences with more fervently progressive elements in the Chinese Democratic League, dialogue between these two main blocs has remained civil and agreeable owing to the members of both having been united in the struggle against despotism in Sichuanese Federalism's earliest days.§!\n
Grand Republican Alliance - United Federal Autonomy Association (Gonghe Datongmeng Zizhi Lianhe Hui)
GRA-CGPS
$SZC_gra_cgps_long_tt$\n§L$GXC_GRA_intro$\n\nWith the integration of many key figures from the Sichuanese Baoding Department and other figures whom many idealists of the Federalist movement would consider merely opportunists, those who sought to consolidate their positions in this new government have rallied around the seasoned general Liu Wenhui and his Civil Governance and Progress Society. Composed of Liu's militarist colleagues like Deng Xihou and Tian Songyao as well as the general's comrades from his own family and patronage networks like the infamous landlord Liu Wencai, these men are all ostensibly members for the goals of self-preservation and have little to no interest in the principles of a genuine democracy.\n\nAs the head of the CGPS, Liu, to the surprise of many of his detractors, has aimed to promote policies of fresh administration and new educational methods, but has found his efforts constantly subverted and co-opted by many of his nominal allies. Deng, in particular, has been increasingly vocal about his own vision for China's modernisation, espousing populist rhetoric and the importance of decisive action over the trappings of democratic discussion.§!\n
Grand Republican Alliance - Civil Governance and Progress Society (Gonghe Datongmeng Minzhi Jingjinshe)
Zhili Clique
$SZC_Zhili_Clique_Civilian_party_long_tt$\n§LOwing its origins to the titanic rise of Feng Guozhang, the Zhili Clique would coalesce around him and his Presidency wherein he advocated for Unification by Negotiation with the South, as opposed to Prime Minister Duan Qirui's Unification by Subjugation. Following Feng's death in 1919, the Zhili Clique would become split between three endeavouring warlords — Cao Kun, Wu Peifu and Wang Chengbin. Engaging in rivalries with the Fengtian and Anhui Cliques, the Zhili Clique would reign supreme in 1922.\n\nDominating the Beiyang Republic for years, the Zhili would experience a climactic fall from power after a war between Qi Xieyuan and Lu Yongxiang would evolve into the Second ZhiFeng War, where Feng Yuxiang, a Zhili member at the time, would betray the clique and launch the 1924 Beijing Coup, ejecting President Cao and Wu Peifu. Whilst briefly regaining their power in an interregnum, it would appear that the Zhili have been ejected from the Central Plains altogether. Without directly intervening on either side in the League Collapse, the Zhili would open themselves to a coup from the detested Royal Court. Resulting in the death of both the primary and secondary leader of the Zhili Clique, it would fall under the tertiary leader, Marshal Wang Chengbin, to wage the fighting retreat to Sichuan province.\n\nNegotiating an agreement with Yang Sen, the Remnant Zhili Clique would see its patronage network severely cut down, with many dying in the Central Plains fighting. Now coalescing around esteemed diplomat Yan Huiqing, the intelligent and quizzical man has proven himself a capable rallying point upon which the civilian bureaucracy can pose a viable alternative to the dominance of Wang's militarists. Jointly united, the Civilians hope to see a reformed Beiyang, as to prevent such a calamity from ever happening again.§!\n
Zhili Clique (Civilian Wing) (Beijing Zhixi (Wenguan Pai))

Baoding Influence
The Baoding Department handles a significant amount of work within the government and the influence it holds lowers our legitimacy significantly. Despite this, their added efforts to our ranks help us ensure the Sichuanese powder-keg doesn't explode.
Internal Divisions
The past decade saw a small decrease in internal divisions of the Sichuan Clique, but the problem still lingers on. The influential Baoding Department, the strong Liu Xiang led faction of the Accelerated Department and the young Officer Department have all set the stage for the province's collapse being imminent at the slight upset of power.
Looming Agricultural Crisis
The production of opium has become extremely pervasive within Sichuan, being one of the few profitable crops due to the province's economic isolation. As a consequence, the production of grain and rice within the province has been reduced to a critical level, a situation made worse by the instability and incompetent governance of the last three decades. Sichuan teeters on the brink of a large-scale famine, were a natural disaster to happen.

Major Famine
A perfect storm of droughts, arable lands being devoted to opium cultivation and the civil war have caused a famine to grip the province of Sichuan. Much like the famine of 1925, the effects on the Sichuanese people is devastating. The state will be partially paralysed until it manages to solve this urgent crisis.

Tax Reform
The modern Chinese Federalist rose and fell across the first half of the 1920s. A coalition of constitutionalists, democrats, and regionalists - they banded together amid the continued North-South stalemate at the peak of the warlord era. Their calls for the various provinces to work towards implementing local self-government and then peacefully unite together into a federal republic achieved some traction, but after a promising start it was rejected by both northern and southern governments. The Zhili's successful unification by force discredited the movement, and many came to associate the movement as little more than a front for warlordism.\n\nRebuilding the momentum that was lost over a decade ago will be difficult, but the with the country once again seemingly hopelessly divided and the Zhili clique's liberalising efforts proving to be a sham, many hold out hope that the Federalist movement could be the solution to China's problems. Whilst few expect much from the often divided Sichuan Cliques, they bear the banner of last stand of Chinese Federalism.

Last Stand of Chinese Federalism: §SDemocratic Reconstruction§!
The modern Chinese Federalist rose and fell across the first half of the 1920s. A coalition of constitutionalists, democrats, and regionalists - they banded together amid the continued North-South stalemate at the peak of the warlord era. Their calls for the various provinces to work towards implementing local self-government and then peacefully unite together into a federal republic achieved some traction, but after a promising start it was rejected by both northern and southern governments. The Zhili's successful unification by force discredited the movement, and many came to associate the movement as little more than a front for warlordism.\n\nChina is a nation of workers, peasants, and intellectuals; to build a civil workplace democracy for the masses is no easy task. Each individual requires their own special needs, and the nation requires that it be able to practice its Four Civic Rights. By fulfilling the principles of self-governance, development of production and improvement of the lives of the epasants and workers, advancement of China's national culture and development of its scientific spirit, it is hoped that the nation shall advance towards the democratic ideal.
Last Stand of Chinese Federalism: §gDemocracy's Five Spirits§!
The modern Chinese Federalist rose and fell across the first half of the 1920s. A coalition of constitutionalists, democrats, and regionalists - they banded together amid the continued North-South stalemate at the peak of the warlord era. Their calls for the various provinces to work towards implementing local self-government and then peacefully unite together into a federal republic achieved some traction, but after a promising start it was rejected by both northern and southern governments. The Zhili's successful unification by force discredited the movement, and many came to associate the movement as little more than a front for warlordism.\n\nMuch like Modernity retains its Five Spirits of Science, Endurance, Aspiration, Loyalty and Public Duty, and Research, Democracy too has its own Five Spirits. That of the Sharing of Governmental Power, Assurance of Freedoms, Protection of Rights, Industrial Health, and that of Cultivation. China clearly aspires to achieve both Democracy and Modernity, but one cannot have the former without the latter, and China is sorely lacking in Modernity. Until it reaches that of a modern industrialised nation-state, the nation's democracy must be taken care of, planned under the auspices of the Civil Governance and Progress.
Last Stand of Chinese Federalism: §lInstitutional Anti-Partisanship§!
The modern Chinese Federalist rose and fell across the first half of the 1920s. A coalition of constitutionalists, democrats, and regionalists - they banded together amid the continued North-South stalemate at the peak of the warlord era. Their calls for the various provinces to work towards implementing local self-government and then peacefully unite together into a federal republic achieved some traction, but after a promising start it was rejected by both northern and southern governments. The Zhili's successful unification by force discredited the movement, and many came to associate the movement as little more than a front for warlordism.\n\nIt is sorely necessary that the nation move beyond its fracture past of the Warlord Era, and onto new beginnings. The world has progressed whilst China has torn itself apart, and much work must be done for the Middle-Kingdom to match the pace of its fellow Nation-States. Now the nation must focus on itself, and on its own development, and through Reapproachement and Dialogue, the nation's institutions must be beyond petty political squabbles; this is the assertion of the new China, a nation for all walks of life.
Martialing of the Vindicated
China gazes upon the abyss, and it stares back. Chinese Federalism, long out of its prime of the 1920s, has been left without root, bequeathed upon its most unlikely son: Xiong Kewu. Marching out of his Tongren hovel in Guizhou, the ambitious general has made it his mission to assure one last final triump for in-which his fellows have failed, or otherwise. Joined in large part by allies of the moment within the Baoding and Officer Departments, and stewarded ultimately by the Third Force Democrats, Chinese Federalism's military arm has largely shaped itself upon the disciplined and rugged soldiers of the nation's interior.
Industrial Autonomy
If China is to succeed on its own two feet, the nation cannot have its already locally producing industries corralled into some sort of national conglomerates and monopolies. The provincial unit is sacred, and thus their industries must be granted autonomy from the national government to conduct business and to develop on their own terms, at least, with necessary worker's provisions enforced.
Start of the Golden Decades
The nation is on the up and up! With the nation receiving some assured stability ever since the Zhili Collapse, investors have begun to return in droves, hoping to cash-in on the rapidly developing Chinese market. With its rich natural resources, massive population, and clever management, China is sure to be the world's next greatest power, as long as growth continues.
Obscurations on Military Loyalties
What should've been foreseen, has ultimately struck the Government of National Reconstruction as its worst betrayal yet. Beholden to promises of National Demobilisation, yet attempting to thrust such an order under a de-jure Warlord backed stratocracy under the surface, the Government has found itself utterly doubting even the loyalties of its own forces. Behold more to their local commanders than the President, the national army is utterly factionalised beyond repair, and serious efforts will need to be taken to remedy such a travesty.
Nonsensical Economic Situation
Hardly capable of being blamed on the Government, China's economic situation, for lack of better wording, is terrible. Ruined by years of mismanagement, perhaps even treading back unto the Qing, the following decades of civil strife, warfare, and foreign exploitation certainly did not benefit the Chinese masses. With investors fleeing following the War with Japan, and the nation more devastated than ever, China's economic situation is paltry, and as ever, the people look towards the Central Government for aid.
Increasing Political Instability
Is it better to hold to your promises, at great cost to oneself? Or betray your fellows in order to preserve stability? For the Government of National Reconstruction, it is the former. Promising National Elections upon unification of the nation and fulfilment of their mission, the Government has begun to tear itself apart; already having been intensely disorganised and unstable. Former allies must now face off against each other, preparing for a political duel for national stewardship, all the while, forces gather in the shadows, gearing themselves to \
No Preparation Too Rigorous!
We have come so far in our quest for unification, and with our sights set upon the Northeast and Japan's other holdings, war with the Empire of the Rising Sun seems all but inevitable. But we shall be ready! Every man must be willing to give their all for our victory and China shall no longer be kept down by Japan like it has since 1895!
The Chinese Determination
Of course, the fate of the Chinese nation and our future can only be shaped through our determination alone - our willingness to work, to fight, to resist and to prosper. As our nation calls upon us, we shall answer, not only for it, but for the brothers and sisters we stand shoulder to shoulder with!
The Republic of China Navy
The precursor to a modern Chinese republican navy dates back to the early days of the Xinhai Revolution when the Ministry of the Navy was formed in the Provisional Government of the Republic of China. The former Qing Dynasty admiral Liu Guanxiong became the first Minister of Navy during this turbulent period. Following the Warlord Era and the subsequent Xuantong Restoration, many elements of the Republic of China Navy fled south for the Kuomintang and Federalist strongholds, while many others chose to remain loyal to the government in Beijing. With the Chinese country finally nominally unified under one banner, the time has come once more to revitalise and rebuild the Republic of China Navy so that it is truly worthy of protecting China's great maritime interests.
The Republic of China Airforce
While initial air operations began with the Qing Dynasty's Beijing Nanyuan airfield - the Republic of China Air Force owes its origins to the various independent air programs proposed and propagated by local warlords, and the Central Government. With our industrial and military strength stronger than ever before, the task is now thrust upon us to continue the legacy left behind by those before us and to create a truly powerful and modern air force for the Chinese people.
Rectifying Economic Disaster
Sichuan has only truly known peace fleetingly and sporadically from Xinhai until now, but it has entered peace again, hopefully in steady enough hands that it won't descend further into chaos. Our priorities can and should now be turned to the worsening socio-economic situation of this province's people, bestowing upon them the path towards prosperity and abundance we have promised for so long.
Abolishing Abominable Tax Practices
A prominent feature of Sichuan's warlord melee was the exorbitant taxes, not only on a litany of things, but also collected well in advance to satiate the volatile monetary demands that financed warlord armies in the Red Basin. But we shall see to things differently, regulating these taxes and finding other revenue sources, so that the people may be relieved of such a tremendous burden.
On the Great Campaign
As the last hope of the federalist movement, it is only right that we turn our focus to realising our true potential and prepare to push outside of our borders against the forces of sheer despotism that may well annihilate us first.
Flourishing Academic Scene
Academic professionals and students, particularly in Sichuan and the derelict western provinces, have long been sidelined in favour of more pressing issues. But due to our moves to support both the students and teachers as of late, our reforms have proven quite successful as the youth of today are shaped into the expertise of tomorrow.
Fighting Societal Apathy
Across all of China but having been particularly salient in Sichuan, the populace, ever occupied with more urgent matters of survival, has had little time to care about the broader movement of politics. This apathy must be tackled at the root, as true democracy cannot expect to survive if it is attacked by the unending cynicism of society from the start.
Establishing Bicameral Legislation
Now that the government, the opposition and various other civic groups organise themselves, the proper details of the legislature must also be ironed out. Zhang Lan's proposal of a bicameral legislature has been a model unanimously agreed upon, and thus will be how all politics shall be carried forward, as long as these democratic institutions exist.
Cemented Delegation of Powers
Along with the structure of the legislature and incoming administration being decided, we should take steps to naturally ensure that adequate checks and balances are in place to free us from the clutches of autocracy moving forward.
Seeing to Domestic Student Demands
Particularly in the more republican movements of both the Kuomintang and the Federalists, the student masses have long been both a supporting force and the main vanguard. As such, we must try to placate some of their demands in return, though we should also try to come to a compromise in the more radical areas.
Two Lius' War
Accelerated Modernisation
Accelerated Army Development
Legitimacy of the Republic: §oDespondent§!
Oh the irony of it all. Having originally been enunciated through the acquiescence of Empress Dowager Longyu, on behalf of Boy Emperor Puyi, the Beiyang Republic was formed in 1912 after the bloody struggle and sacrifices of legions of martyrs for the eradication of the monarchy. Bounding with hope and optimism, the people marched forward under the banners of reformers and revolutionaries alike, experiencing the great equalisation and pluralisation of the new, young and malleable republic. Yet it would all be snuffed out following the machinations of a despot. Having torn itself apart through strongmen and warlords, the Beiyang Republic was nothing but a corrupt, incompetent tool hoisted by whatever warlord clique controlled Beijing at the time. Cabinets lasted months, the Governmental system transitioned seven times in its whole existence, and despite it all there was still a sense of hope.\n\nExpelled from its rightful place in Beijing, the Beiyang establishment and the Zhili Clique have been cowed into exile with amicable allies in Sichuan. However that is perhaps one of many mistakes the Royalists have embarked upon. Under the auspices of Marshal Wang Chengbin, the Zhili have recuperated, and with it the legacy of the Xinhai Revolution lives on within them. And yet the common people, the common masses, and some of our estranged allies, doubt how genuine our sentiments are. Given that the Zhili tossed away the Republic when it was convenient, many believe our nation-state building project to be a sham. Although they would be wrong, for the only thing on the mind of the Marshal is revenge.

Under their watchful eye, the technocratic administration remains pumping ever more, maintaining the gears of politics and administration. Under their light a new, reformed, Republic descends. One that claims legacy from the Xinhai political order, yes, but one that has seen it transformed into a new, truly diligent machine. A republic, not controlled by militarists or warlords, but one that works with them, hand-in-hand.

The Jade Marshal may very well be peering at the Zhili with dismay, but the burden of leadership has been placed upon Wang's shoulders now.

The Five Races Under One Union, it's legacy of national pride, patriotism and unification, it shall forever fly with national pride! A new hope and optimism finally arrives for the Chinese people. \
Legitimacy of the Republic: §6Tianjin's Democracy§!
Oh the irony of it all. Having originally been enunciated through the acquiescence of Empress Dowager Longyu, on behalf of Boy Emperor Puyi, the Beiyang Republic was formed in 1912 after the bloody struggle and sacrifices of legions of martyrs for the eradication of the monarchy. Bounding with hope and optimism, the people marched forward under the banners of reformers and revolutionaries alike, experiencing the great equalisation and pluralisation of the new, young and malleable republic. Yet it would all be snuffed out following the machinations of a despot. Having torn itself apart through strongmen and warlords, the Beiyang Republic was nothing but a corrupt, incompetent tool hoisted by whatever warlord clique controlled Beijing at the time. Cabinets lasted months, the Governmental system transitioned seven times in its whole existence, and despite it all there was still a sense of hope.\n\nFinally he has done it. After the struggles, the great perennial trials, the continuous hardship, the great, magnificent Marshal of Tianjin has overseen the restoration of the Beiyang Republic, and the unification of the nation! Whilst many feared he would be a mere continuation of the military despots that have toyed with the Republic's institutions since its inception, the Marshal has no pretences of his own superiority over the Republic. With his mission concluded, and the nation stabilised, a new era of democracy in China may begin to develop. Under his watchful eye, of course.
All for the Reconquest!
If we are to ever see our beautiful Beijing again, we must first and foremost dedicate every single resource available in Sichuan to our grand and glorious campaign. For the reclamation of our glorious Republic is an arduous task, one demanding the absolute most of every single Chinese patriot within our lands. No matter the cost.
Assistance of the German Giant
The last bulwark of Zhili prosperity, Sichuan province is far from a sustainable home for the institutions of the Republic, nor its expensive and modern military arm. Utilising our latent contacts within the German Legations, presuming they've not burnt all of our bridges, we have invited a series of military industrial manufacturers to promulgate new Accelerated factories within our homebase. With this, it is hoped that the reclamation of our rightful land will arrive soon enough.
Increasing Pluralisation
Following our enabling of further political participation in the exiled assembly, it would appear that the people have begun to become politically minded, swayed by the wise words of our politicians. Providing much needed legitimacy and stability for our government's apparatus, it has also led to an increase in popular support for the opposition parties within the rump Assembly.
Legacy of Baoding and Luoyang
The Baoding and Luoyang Cliques, now functionally extinct due to the decapitation of their leadership, carried with them austere and sincere air of warlords transforming into politicians. Foregoing the sabre and rifle for the suit and tie, they were in earnest Chinese statesmen. Cut short with the awful coup d'état, it has fallen to the Tianjin Clique, and the remnants of the others, alongside the clique of Beiyang bureaucrats to continue their mission of sincere statesmanship.
Embracing Meritocracy
Perhaps one of our greatest follies is that of the Zhili's patronage network. A reclusive association of nepotistic relationships disguised as good Confucian practices, it has resulted in a high command that is increasingly isolated, and a discontent lower sect of officers. Many of those officers aided the Manchus in the coup, in the hopes of receiving their due promotion. To truly reform, it must not only be politics, but that of the military's structure too.
Expertise of the Military
Our military of old was that of a miracle worker. Under the guise of the Jade Marshal's military brilliance, it performed tasks inconceivable, and feats that were nigh impossible. Of course that was in-part due to the military genius of Wu Peifu. Whilst Marshal Wang is surely not a fool, he is not a God of War either. To succeed, we must re-examine our doctrines, for all facets of warfare.
The 1923 Cao Kun Constitution
A remarkable piece of progressive legislature, the 1923 Cao Kun Constitution perhaps represents the peak of Beiyang idealism and hope in the merits of the Zhili Clique. Ultimately receiving a pluralist support from the majority of the Northern Assemblymen at the time, the Cao Kun constitution marked a significant attempt to formalise proper governance in the Beiyang Republic following a tumultuous era of blatant abuses by Duan Qirui and his Anfu Club. Seeking to establish a structured, organised and centralised government, it places significant executive power within that of the President. However it features remarkable components such as a clear separation of powers and an outline of clear civil rights of the Chinese people. Rather unfortunately, its implementation a decade ago was marred by allegations of corruption and autocracy, having been conducted around the similar timeframe in which Cao's bribery scandal concluded. And yet again, its re-implementation in this new era of chaotic times signals another attempt to rapidly stabilise the political situation. Rife with potential loopholes for executive abuse, one must merely place faith in the institutions at this current time to truly exert the will of the people.
Providing Bread and Circuses
To truly win the hearts of the people, it would not be prudent to toss meaningless concepts of \
Embracing Militarism
For our own national salvation, it requires the participation of every single citizen's martial spirit in order for an overseeing of the revival of the militaristic nation-state. Under the auspices of General Jiang Baili, the people are undergoing a revival of their own bushido, their own capacity for self-sacrifice for the motives of an ulterior goal. Greater than the individual, we must reclaim the spirit of the nation.
Legacy of the Academies
Deprived of Baoding, deprived of Kunming, the militarists are without the very cradles of their cliques. Nonetheless, we must carry on, with or without their expertise. For the majority of our officers and commanders are descendants of the martial spirit invoked in such institutions, and we'd be damned if we forgot our origins now.
Dawn of the Final Offensive
It is upon us! The hour of judgement! A true test of our new, reformed capabilities! Now is the time of great struggle, for our enemies lord over our rightful national capital, and if we are to fail, the Zhili Clique as we know it will perish. The Beiyang Republic does not linger on under the auspices of that perfidious Old Marshal, but under the Marshal of Tianjin! Zhonghua Mingguo Wansui!
Old Hope and Glory
Our men grow tired, their morale plummets, our factories halt, and our workers lament. The absolute dedication of every manageable resource to our total victory has come with an unduly cost. Whilst it will depart with time, the strain, the tears, they lie with our nation, seeping into its ground. One can only hope the sacrifices were worth it.
Hundred Years War of Resistance
The invaders dare trespass on our territory! The foreign imperialists, the vile Japanese! They have arrived to finally seize and eradicate our nation in a war of national survival! Every man, women and child must truly dedicate themselves in body and spirit to the preservation of China's millennia old civilisation, for we must prove to the Japanese that we can wage a Hundred Years War of Resistance!
Sounding the Bugles of Victory
Finally we have done it! The grand reclamation of the Zhili Clique's rightful position within the Chinese nation-state. No more shall we be forced to co-exist with the perfidious monarchists, no more shall we bow to any foreign power! The Zhili Clique may have been deposed, it may have initially lost its leadership, but it has found a new soul in the likes of Marshal Wang and Yan Huiqing. The bugles of victory sound, and the people rejoice!
Extending a Hand to the Young China
Despite their convictions and reluctant participation in the Manchu bureaucracy, the Young China Party at its core is that of a nationalist, patriotic and devoutly Republican one. Whilst we were at odds before, many within the Assembly and the soldiery view their ideological tenacity with pride. Whilst hardliners would rather see them excise, cooperating once more with the YCP can see a reinvigoration of Chinese militarism and nationalism.
Intellectualism with Endeavour
The Endeavour Society, a long functioning intellectual organisation and article producer, was founded under the likes of Cai Yuanpei, Hu Shih, Li Dazhao, Liang Shuming, Wang Chonghui, Tao Menghe and many other reformist, later revolutionary in certain cases, intellectuals. Continuously championed by Hu Shih in some form, they represent one of the many Federalist blocs within the North's political scene. Sharing a mutual home during our exile, let us further integrate this think tank further into our government, however they expect much of our government. Most importantly, immediate reform of its institutions.
The Public Safety Bureau
The Public Safety Bureau, or PSB, is the name of the Intelligence Agency moonlighting as the Zhili's secret police, nominally led by Liu Menggeng and Wang Yujia. Utilising both their contacts within the Central Plains and elsewhere alongside their admirable experience in running Cao Kun's spy and intelligence rings, the entity has been established to ensure that the possibility of a Manchu Coup could never happen again. Espionage, suppression of internal dissent and counter-intelligence are just some of the many objectives the institution has been authorised to deal with.
Behind Manchu Lines
They may have squashed our military might on the surface, but little do the Royalists know that the Zhili networks and influence seeps deep into the earth of the Central Plains. Our beloved King of Baoding may have been mercilessly slaughtered at the hands of the Manchu Princes, but his networks remain forever strong. And willing to leverage us any benefit for the annihilation of our enemy.
Reconstituting the Beiyang Navy
Following through with a rather ambitious plan drawn up by restored Minister of the Navy, Admiral Sa Zhenbing, a significant portion of the country's budget is being prioritised for a state-planned modernisation and production effort of a brand new fleet of ships. It is hoped that by the end of this year plan, the Chinese Navy will have rapidly modernised, and will no longer sail ships of a decade before.
Western Revitalisation Plan
Encourage Local Initiative
Crafting Talent of the New Generation
The most crucial element in developing China in our path to modernity is to properly educate the masses. As the masses learn the skills of the modern age, so too shall more of the people partake in the political system, and shore up our newfound democracy. We seek an educated populace guiding our Republic forward!
Vaulting Militaristic Personalism
During the Chinese Civil War, various prominent warlords rose to great influence within the Federal military. These warlords command a force loyal not primarily loyal to the Republic, but to their commanding officer. If our Republic's democracy is to thrive, personalism must be rooted out from the source.
Government Union Partnership
Trade unions haven't been the most prominent force in China, primarily owing to the nation's agrarian nature that had been the norm for so long. However, as unification is achieved and Chinese industry takes the lead, workers must also gain representation. We must expand and integrate the unions so that workers from the silk farms of Sichuan, to the coal mines of Shanxi, and to the docks of Shanghai get their say.
China's Industrial Revolution
Having been embroiled in a plethora of turmoils until now, China has been a land split between subsistence farming in the west and various derelict industries in the East. But no longer! By educating our people on the benefits of industry and how to operate and construct, we shall seek to industrialise at a rapid speed, leveraging our previously untapped resources. We shall rival Britain in a decade's time!
Specialised Practical Schools
Forming from examples pioneered in Nanchong, specialised practical schools have been established, with schools acquiring professional classes for training on matters of agriculture and sericulture, both integral industries, especially in Sichuan. More schools have also begun to introduce professional classes for science, liberal arts, traditional Chinese medicine, and heavy industry. Each of these specialised classes features its own practical workshops, farms, and clinical internships, promoting the integration of education and productive labour.
Finding a Use for All
National Centralisation is required, no time more so than right now, as China finally mostly falls under a new administration. Former political figures, whether they be politician or warlord, must be given work in productive developments lest they do nothing but obstruct and criticise the government. Similarly, the unemployed and idle must be pressed into technical programs to prepare them for China's industrial future, and all technical expertise must be utilised.
The National Demobilisation Programme
Now that unification is upon us, the issue of militarisation can once again be addressed. Excessive and runaway mobilisation by multiple actors has always been a problem across both Sichuan and Warlord China more generally. The time has come to standardise standing armies and drastically reduce the size of irregular and autonomous military formations, as we have promised the people from the start.
New Style Education Scheme
Lack of widespread education has always been the root of cultural backwardness throughout China, having been observed first-hand by General Liu Wenhui during his time in Sichuan. No doubt, the status quo needs reform - new public examinations must be organised, demonstration meetings must be hosted, and the top of the student cohorts are to be selected for more prestigious posts and commended for their achievements.
True Purposes of Knowledge: Civic Democracy
In order to move forward with the times, education must continually evolve to meet the demands of modernity. The lingering poison of the old imperial examination mindset must be dealt with!As educators and cultural workers, we have a historic duty: we must proclaim a declaration of intellectual independence, secure for students the freedom to learn, research, speak, and publish, and thereby complete the democratisation of educational spirit.
True Purposes of Knowledge: National Sacrifice
In order to move forward with the times, education must continually evolve to meet the demands of modernity. The lingering poison of the old imperial examination mindset must be dealt with! People ought not to think of pursuing education as a stepping-stone to high offices and riches. We must find ways for our brightest minds to devote themselves, within fifty years, not to becoming doctors of literature or philosophy, but to the study of raising livestock and agricultural cultivation - a true education of the people.

Famine Relief Efforts
The famine that wreaked havoc on Sichuan in 1925 has left a deep scar upon our people. While we've done what we can to prevent another one, the collapse of the League, persistent drought and rampant unrest has turned our worst fears into reality. We must now do everything we can to fight this famine.\n\n§1The famine will end when its §Y$MODIFIER_GLOBAL_MONTHLY_POPULATION$§! modifier reaches §!§Y0%§! (currently [?SZC_famine_monthly_population|=%+0]).\n\nCurrent Relief Resources: £convoy_texticon  [?SZC_famine_PP|H0]
International Famine Relief
China has endured a lot in recent years and there is only so much we can do to help ourselves. In places abroad, that have not been blighted by war or famine, there's more than enough grain to go around. We should appeal for them to help us in our time of need.
Service for Food
Every able-bodied man that can serve must do his part to overcome the disaster! As such, we'll offer civilians increased rations in exchange for military service and have these soldiers assist in the distribution of food to the masses.
Labour Relief
There isn't enough food to go around, so those that can must work to earn their rations. We'll set up a programme where the unemployed and able-bodied are conscripted as labourers and paid in rations to build the infrastructure and facilities we need to better combat the famine.
Allocate More Government Funds
In order to fight the famine, we'll need to step in with more resources from the government. This will, however, come at the expense of other state projects.
Increase Relief Efforts
It's clear that more must be done to distribute the food into the countryside. Local leaders in rural parts of Sichuan will be tasked with setting up programmes to distribute rice to their communities.
Food Banks
The government will work with farmers and Buddhist temples to bring food to the people of Sichuan, better helping us reach every level of society with our efforts to combat this disaster.
Subsidise Food Production
Sichuan has plenty of farmers, but since most of them don't earn enough to rely on anything but the weather and antiquated methods the spectre of a new famine looms with every drought. By stepping in with money from its own coffers, the state can help farmers combat waste and increase productivity.
Enact Price Controls
When the famine broke out many merchants started to hoard grain and rice while charging extortionate fees for these goods. The state, backed by the army if need be, will make sure no one profiteers from the misery of our people by enacting price controls.
Child Protection Programme
Fading Famine
With the end of the drought, our agriculture has started to slowly recover. Over the next months, the catastrophic famine will finally fade into the past... leaving only its scars behind.

[From.GetNameDef]
Since drought has rendered the yield of most of our farmlands meagre at best for the foreseeable future, the state will allocate funds to import food from abroad, to make up for what the drought destroyed.

the Central Government

the Legation Council
From Hong Kong to Shanghai, the Legation Cities possess an abundance of wealth and resources. Compared to the rest of China, they're largely left unscathed by the death of Marshal Sun and the subsequent turmoil. Because of this, they're in a position to help - whether their bureaucracy is willing to, however, is another matter altogether.
Sales Monopoly Bureau
The opium situation is beyond our control at this point and we're in no position to completely rid ourselves from it. Instead of eradicating the industry entirely, we'll bring it under the control of the state and put the profits from this vice into our coffers.\n\nCurrent Opium Control: £opium_texticon  [?SZC_opium_control|+%1]
Bureaucratic Reforms
We need to take measures to mould the state bureaucracy into functioning less like a conventional one and more like a business as far as opium is concerned. By making gradual changes to this effect, we'll streamline our control over the market.
Buy Out Merchants
Sometimes the best way to deal with the competition is to simply buy it out. While a costly investment for the state to make, in due time these costs to our state coffers should be paid back through the profits we'll make.
Forced Acquisitions
By adopting a very literal interpretation of the law, we can send in the police to forcibly shut down a few private markets and use their goods and property to expand our monopoly.
Tax Harvesting Scheme
In order to increase revenues to fund our government plans, we can devote extra resources to local administrators and help their efforts to collect the taxes - old, current and new - owed to us and squeeze out every penny from those that thought they were above the law. It'll be unpopular, but it's for the good of Sichuan.
Transit Tariffs
We'll have the military and police establish checkpoints throughout the key roads and transit points around Sichuan to tax the transportation of opium. While a hassle for the commoner, it'll fill our coffers and prevent the competition from moving their goods.
Farmer Licensing
Every farm engaging in opium production will need a licence to operate from here on. Failure to comply will, of course, force us to confiscate their property.
Uncontested Monopoly
There is no more opium market in Sichuan, only a state monopoly that the criminals and smugglers can't touch. If they aren't directly under our control, they're de facto so through our regulations and taxes. While some may say that we're no better than the criminals we ousted, we've brought security and a steady stream of money to the state.
Combat Corruption
Our efforts to maintain market control are hampered by some of our officials taking bribes in order to turn a blind eye to the non-sanctioned opium businesses. By removing them, there'll be fewer cracks for the non-state actors to slip through.
Combat Smuggling
By diverting our army to patrol the roads and rivers of the country we'll be able to greatly hinder the smugglers cutting into the state's monopoly. Gradually, this will drive them out of business.
Opium Prohibition Committee
Since the Treaty of Tianjin was imposed upon us, the opium trade has ravaged China and brought despair to millions of Chinese. Our guilt in this is significant - Sichuan is the rotten core of this destructive industry. The challenge facing the Opium Prohibition Committee is immense, but we owe it to our people to free them from the clutches of opium.\n\nCurrent Opium Spread: £opium_texticon  [?SZC_opium_spread|+%1]
Promote Crop Production
One of the reasons for the prevalence of opium crops is their profitability. By subsidising and otherwise promoting the growth of regular crops we should start seeing more of our farmers move away from growing opium.
Poppy Burning Campaign
We'll cut the supply off right at the source by sending the army to raid some of the more prominent illegal opium fields still in operation.
Prohibitionist Victory
Through the dedication of the OPC, the scourge of addiction that has plagued Sichuan for so long is finally contained and those profiteering from it are behind bars or chased out of our provinces. This is truly a victory worth celebrating!
Anti-Corruption Campaigns
Our efforts in containing the spread of opium are greatly hindered by corrupt officials and civil servants that take bribes, embezzle funds and ignore the law when convenient. More efforts should be taken to make sure they know that their badges and titles don't make them stand above the law
Purge the Administration
Drastic times call for drastic measures and we presently have too many weasels in our midst that profiteer from our people's hardships. We'll use our police and army to remove them from their positions and send a clear message that we will not tolerate corruption.
Anti Smuggling Measures
By diverting our army to patrol the roads and rivers of the country we'll be able to greatly reduce the freedom of movement of the smugglers in our province.
Break the Black Market
Instead of gradually suppressing the criminals, we'll send in the army and fight them like we would fight any other enemy of Sichuan with unrestricted force.
§RThe bandits won't take this one lying down. If this operation is a failure, it'll significantly set back our efforts!§!
Set Up Treatment Clinics
By building new clinics and expanding existing ones to rehabilitate the addicted, we'll mitigate the effects of the crisis and make the business less profitable for smugglers.
§GOnce the crisis is over, these clinics will still be around to help people with more conventional needs.§!
The Diarchy
Unlike many warlord cliques in China, Baoding is noted for being more prone to cooperation than competition. If the balance is maintained it'll bring powerful benefits to Sichuan. Both sides need to give and take for the cooperation to work, for if one side becomes too dominant the diarchy may start to resemble the autocracies that surround it.
Favour the Militarists
By supporting the more conservative military wing through funding and favours, our army will reap the benefits while giving their faction a boost in the public eye. If the army is neglected, it'll degrade their performance in the field. Letting them grow too strong, however, risks crippling Sichuan's civilian branches of government. While it's certainly tempting to favour the army in times of war in particular, we should be careful not to provoke a hostile response by letting our administrative duties crumble.
Favour the Bureaucrats
By providing more resources and public support for the civilian branches of government, we'll see an well-oiled bureaucracy, more able to tackle the challenges that the province faces. Should we favour them too heavily, however, our army will suffer the results of spending cuts and perform worse in the field. If this goes on for too long, we can't rule out the army taking measures into their own hands to adjust this imbalance.
Send Help to the League
Zhili Remnants
The Zhili remnants, under the auspices of §PMarshal Wang Chengbin§! have managed to recuperate their forces within [SZC.Capital.GetCapitalVictoryPointName]. However brutally beaten, losing many good men along the way, the Remnant Zhili Forces join our native Sichuan armies as a spent force. On the bright side, all is not lost. With veterans from the ZhiFeng Wars, and intense experience fighting the Manchu armies in their withdrawal, the men are skilled, hardy and all too capable. We should seek to integrate and reform the Zhili forces, so that we can strike back on the war path against the Royalists, anyone else who dares stand in our way of national unification.
Reorganise the Remnant Divisions
Fleeing with a retinue of his most loyal, diehard soldiers, §PMarshal Wang Chengbin§! alongside the likes of Jiang Baili and Zhang Qihuang bring with them their remnant forces that, used to, comprise the majority of their divisions. Once the Central Army, the Zhili are now reduced to a paltry force, outer Zhili members such as Tang Xiangming, or the League non-withstanding. Perhaps a costly endeavour, the §PMarshal§! has constructed a plan in-which the forces will be demobilised, reorganised and reconstituted into a group of elite \
Foreign Arms Deals
Devout in our crusade against the Manchu and their royalists, this does not necessarily mean we are opposed to the practices and convictions of the imperialists. Not quite yet. After all, one thing at a time, no? Whilst our noble armament arsenals such as Chongqing and Daxian work around the clock to produce the artillery, the shells, the bullets and the rifles necessary to sustain our armies, another avenue for armaments has defined itself. Far reduced from our stature as the Central Government, internationally recognised, that does not matter in the scale of the arms trade. Looking towards a wider expanse of benefactors in the international arms area, we can arm ourselves for the great reconquest!
Purchase Foreign Guns
With the increasing military modernisation around the globe, clearly in preparation for some broader national conflict on the horizon, international rifles are being rapidly modernised similarly. Resulting in an influx of outdated designs gathering dust in global stockpiles, our logistics staff have drafted a series of contracts in which we would purchase an assortment of excess armaments.
Purchase Foreign Support Equipment
A surprising hotbed of armament manufacturing and design, the Danish Madsen Machine Gun has proven itself an undeniably reliable, effective and wonderful support light machine gun for not just our soldiers, but that of armies in the here and now. The world's first true light machine gun produced in quantity, the military command staff has taken a particular liking to the Dane's support weaponry.
Purchase Foreign Artillery
A curious choice amongst our other potential military armament benefactors, the Swiss military industrial complex has nonetheless remained an admirable, if modest, national industry. With their neutrality ever present however, their equipment usually ends up for sale on the international weapons market. All too familiar with the fact that artillery is king in Chinese warfare, the Army would be all too delighted to receive modern guns, in significant quantity for once.
Hire Russian Civil War Veterans
With our relationship with Germany tenuous at best, and other imperialists distant due to our lack of legitimacy, many believe that our grand ambitions for a reconquest are bereft of assistance in military development. Yet there remains one Western, modern nation that has yet to openly oppose us as of recent. Russia.\n\nGranted, many despise the Russian Bear due to their previous colonial expansionist policies, such as the seizure of Outer Manchuria, or the further invasion of Dongbei in the wake of the Boxer Rebellion. Nonetheless, their disparaged, ambitious and older officers prove themselves incredibly fitting to substitute what the German advisors could provide. Clearly skilled in nearly all facets required of them.
United Anti-Japanese Front
The Rising Sun is upon us! And if China is to survive, it must all come together, no matter what creed, to defend the nation's millennia-old civilisation. With established ties with various leading leftist figures throughout the country, the government could further solicit an alliance with some of the nation's greatest military tacticians and strategists, even if it may cast a downpour on China's bourgeois democracy...
Reconstruct Naval Pride
The Chinese fleet used to be one of the great major fleets of the whole world, ranking seventh in tonnage. Alas, having been sunk into the bottom of the ocean following the Sino-Japanese War, Chinese naval projections have never recovered; eternally cornered by the Rising Sun. With additional leeway following unification of the nation, the remaining naval cliques have pressured the government to finally begin China's grand naval rearmament programme, for the Middle Kingdom is awakening, and it must be able to protect its own waters.
Creating the Chinese Airforce
China's disparate regional airforce programs have overseen muddled or otherwise confused batches of progress over the years. With the most impressive results emerging from the Southwest in Kunming, and the Northeast within Shenyang, other local programs have not been as lucky. Liu Xiang's own native programme within Sichuan for example, used rocks akin to explosive bombs. If China is to be a true great power, it must be able to assert itself within the Third Avenue of Warfare, and thus, can spare no expense in rapidly developing its own air fleet.
Bear the Banner of Federalist Hopes
Despite our assistance, and despite any reasonable resistance to Federalism's enemies, the steward of the Chinese Provincial Autonomy project has fallen to enemy forces who would sooner bring their hammer to bear upon those that aspire for democracy and freedom than yield an inch. With the provincial government's back against the wall, it is time for [SZC.Capital.GetCapitalVictoryPointName] to become China's last haven for Provincial Autonomy.
