A Grandiose Plan
Ever since Liu Xiang was denied the governorship of Sichuan, the Zhili and their lapdogs have done nothing but hold us back. We can only tolerate this for so long. It's high time that [SZC.GetLeader] marched his army into Beijing and shattered them, once and for all - uniting all of China under his rule if he has to.
The Lord of Sichuan
With [SZC.GetLeader]'s undisputed rule over Sichuan now a fact, the age of bickering warlords is finally over. Now that all the pieces are on place and any potential threat to the Accelerated Department has been either destroyed or pacified, we can finally forge ahead and decide Sichuan's fate for ourselves.
Famine Relief Corps
The people - or our soldiers, for that matter - cannot feed themselves from bark, grass and clay. Since the recent civil war created countless prisoners of war from the traitorous factions, we'll offer them the prospect of amnesty in exchange for tilling the fallow fields and preparing the distribution of food. Under close watch of our soldiers, of course.
Accelerated Modernisation
The old regime evidently didn't bother to catch up with the rest of the China. Instead, it clearly neglected its duty to its people and now we're the backwater of China. Our people will need to work hard to make up for the past decade's neglect and we'll make sure it bears fruit.
Fund the Construction Industry
Yang Sen was content to simply lord over fields of opium that wouldn't look out of place in the worst periods of the 19th century. If we are to bring Sichuan into the new era, however, the state will need to invest big in order to make it happen. Spare no expenses today, so that the next generation will be prosperous!
The Riches of Xikang
The wealth of Xikang lays mostly untapped beneath the mountains. We'll need a modern steel industry so that our mighty military can march into battle with the rifles, cannons, vehicles and ships that they need.
Expand Arms Production
The original ambitions of Liu Xiang always accounted for the inevitability of war. The Accelerated Department rose to prominence through conflict, and we're unlikely to bring peace to China without more bloodshed. Whether it's defensive or offensive, we need to arm ourselves for fend off our future foes as well.
Mass Education Campaigns
It wasn't just the cities that were neglected by the old Qing overlords and their stooges, but the minds of Sichuan's people as well. Illiteracy runs rampant and most people are clueless as to their rich history and duty to the state. Our literate officers shall act as teachers and the masses will learn by the millions.
Currency Reform
Before we defeated our rivals, every local province's warlord had their own worthless currency. That is, if they weren't even relegated to an ancient barter economy. Now that we're in charge, it's time we stamp out these vestiges of the past and start to use one united currency for one united Sichuan.
Sichuan Central Bank
Up until recently much of Sichuan's economy has been splintered into various local financial ecosystems under local mayors and warlords. By finally creating a centralised banking system with its beating heart centred in Chongqing we will be able to break this trend and drive our economy in one unified direction.
Standardise Land Tax
The old tax system was a byzantine mess. Depending on which province you were in, it was either broken, inefficient or a governor's attempt to rob the people blind. We'll do away with this nonsense and implement our own centralised tax law, free from the grift and inefficiency of the past.
Urban Expansion
We cannot call ourself a modern nation unless we urbanise. We must encourage people to move in from the countryside and devote everything into expanding our cities. After we're done, Chongqing and Chengdu may well be the envy of Shanghai and Hong Kong!
The Mighty Navy
Our capital of Chongqing rests near the Yangtze River, leaving it rather vulnerable to naval attacks from downriver, but also making it into a perfect base for the future navy of Sichuan. Eventually, a mighty armada of ships shall patrol the rivers, protecting our trade and people from banditry and showing our might to the rest of China.
The Mighty Air Force
Why should we scale the mountains of Sichuan to meet every threat when planes can simply attack them from the air? We'll start by importing foreign technology to use as a base. Once we're done, our air force will be the greatest in all of China, able to protect our skies and strike any foe!
Army Drills
For far too long, the warlords of Sichuan were content with their forces resembling bandits more than actual soldiers. To mark a clear break from this past, the Chongqing high command is preparing for a programme of province-wide army drilling and retraining. With enough effort, we'll have soldiers that are the most disciplined in all of China!
Adopt Radio Communications
Modern wars are increasingly fought with the help of radio, radar and computing machines. It's therefore crucial for our modernisation programme that we procure and develop new advances in these fields and that our forces, down to every company, receive training in their use.
Dedicated Logistics Units
Even after our army becomes the mightiest in China - at least on paper - it'll be helpless in the field without a steady stream of supplies to keep it marching forward. By utilising Chongqing's industry, we'll set up specialised supply trains that will be the envy of all Chinese military planners!
Large Front Operations
The key to winning battles is to properly utilise the vast manpower of Sichuan to wear down and overwhelm our foes. While a common warlord would simply use them as a bludgeon, we'll develop sophisticated methods for using large infantry charges as our spearheads, including the management and rapid deployment of reserves.
Reverse-Engineer Modern Weapons
It'd be a waste to simply distribute the foreign equipment we have acquired to the troops. To make the most of it, we'll dispatch our brightest military engineers to reverse-engineer them so that we can produce our own, superior variants.
Heavy Firepower Tactics
It's clear that we need to double our efforts to produce qualified artillery officers, since many of them still use their batteries in the most rudimentary ways. When we're done reforming our training methods, our artillery will shake the earth itself with mighty barrages ahead of every offensive we launch!
Armament Production Innovations
We cannot call our army truly modernised unless we develop our own modern arms. We'll pour more funds into our military R&D department so that they have the means to produce new weapons, made from the ground up by Chinese hands.
Accelerated Army Development
All our efforts to modernise have borne fruit. Our now mighty army has perfected the fusion of both military and industrial might to overwhelm any foe. Thanks to our industries, we can amass more guns, bullets, bombs and shells to use against our foes than anyone else in China. Let them tremble before the might of the Accelerated Army!
Republican Triumph
Against all odds, the Officer Department has secured control over the provincial government. The two leaders, Xiong Kewu and Lü Chao, are preparing to consolidate their position and make Sichuan a bastion of republicanism and democracy.
Preparing Sichuan for Federalism
Although Xiong stands above all other warlords following the fall of Yang Sen, it would be a mistake to consider his control over Chuan to be absolute. Indeed, the minor warlords of Sichuan have often looked enviously towards the leader of the ensemble, and Xiong Kewu must ensure that his current time in the sun will not be ended prematurely, as it has before.
Establish Fundamental Laws
Sichuan finds itself in a particular dire situation, even relative to its bordering provinces. Decades of civil war within the province and invasions from its neighbours have left much of the province destitute and lawless, and the Xiong administration shall see such chaos cured with order brought about by a far-reaching series of legal reforms and regulations.
Observe the New Guard
In order to break Sichuan's cycle of warlord infighting, the old warlords must be rooted out, reform after reform. The New Sichuan requires officers who understand loyalty to the Xiong administration to be their patriotic duty, and they shall come to fill the ranks of the government over time, while old parasites find themselves retired from the halls of power.
Our Promise to the Province
While Xiong Kewu stands triumphant as Sichuan's governor, the people shall know his solemn promise to the province. Xiong's government seeks to ensure local government from the village will not be trampled upon by opportunistic militarists, the people will work together for a common good, and all classes shall see a new horizon in time.
Solicit Cross-Regional Cooperation
While the Federalist Movement has largely been a southern movement that protests Beijing's centralising tendencies, it must be known that it is not the destruction of the Beiyang Republic which we seek. No, it is our goal to redeem the Republic to be the pillar of hope it was always meant to be, freeing both North and South.
Construct New Arsenals
In this time of great chaos, it is not the pen which brings political power, but the barrel of a gun. While Fengtian wields the Shenyang Arsenal, Beijing can count on the Hanyang Arsenal on its side. If Sichuan is to earn the respect of the major warlords, Xiong must see Sichuan develop an Arsenal of its own.
Inter-Allied Command
Although the minor warlords respect Xiong's right to rule, they guard their own meagre forces zealously. If Sichuan is to become a respectable player in Chinese politics, all the officers of this province must stand together in a unified command structure. Let Sichuan's disunity be turned into a strength!
Legacy of the Nation Building Allied Army
Perhaps the greatest Sichuanese army was the Nation-Building Allied Army, a mighty force led by Xiong in 1925. The province may yet find such heights of success once again, through Xiong's restoration of the Mobile Officer Training School. Once again shall this institution train Sichuan's finest officers, ones who may see the nation unified.
Rule of the Officers
In perhaps the greatest twist of all, the Officers under Li Jiayu and Luo Zezhuo have established themselves as the leaders of Sichuan Province. Obscure underdogs for their entire careers, Li and Luo have established a working relationship with Lü Chao's Industrial Corps, and together these three shall bring Sichuan into a new age.
Overlook Our Excesses
Even amidst our triumph, we must concede the fact that our forces are still relatively inexperienced compared to other provincial forces. One aspect that contributed to our victory was the presence of generals with experience gained from proper academy training or fighting with other armies. As such, it is appropriate that we give these veteran commanders some leeway, overlooking their less relevant attributes, whether they be addicts, unreasonable disciplinarians or both.
Court the Young Soldiers Federation
A minor faction within the Officer Corps coalition, the Young Soldiers Federation is a leftist and populist organisation calling for stronger benefits for soldiers. While the finer details of the movement escape Li, he recognises the benefits in endorsing such a platform for the Officers to promote in Sichuanese governance.
No Demilitarisation Without Militarisation
It is well known to all those under Heaven that Sichuan has toiled under the misfortunes of warlord infighting for decades. While demilitarisation is a dream sought by many, the Officers cannot enforce true demilitarisation while other warlords brandish their swords towards our government, for only the sword can bring peace.
The Source of Our Vigour
Caught between the various warlords who have subjugated them to ruthless exploitation, the peasantry found themselves greatly sympathetic to our meagre cause during the Zhili Decade. It was due to their support that the Officers were able to return to Sichuan in 1936, and the rural masses shall remain our lifeline!
Repaying the Country's Kindness
Even in this tumultuous time, the common people have not forgotten the common virtue which binds us all. As Confucius called upon the state to be the vehicle of the principles and kindness of the people, so shall Li Jiayu's Sichuan stand to be a pillar of virtue in a sea of unjust warlords.
For the National Cause
While Sichuan may have found peace after decades of agonising warfare, the ancestral homeland continues to be defiled by oppressive warmongers. Sichuan stands for the cause of a better Republic, and Li Jiayu lends his blade to the liberation of all China from the yoke of tyranny and imperialism.
Centralise Tax and Customs
In Sichuan's time of disunity, various warlord fiefdoms began to enact drastically divergent policies, which has resulted in a bureaucratic mess for the Officer administration. The administration has begun working towards slashing the various superfluous regional taxes, and establishing a singular province-wide taxation system.
Connect Rural Townships
While the Sichuan basin is a comfortable lowland region that operates as our heartland, the farflung regions of Chuan host treacherous mountains and titanic river systems. To establish authority across the entire province, these rural townships must be reconnected to the basin network.
Raise the Weary, Help the Weak
Truly, the Sichuanese Civil War has brought about untold suffering on the people. Many families find themselves torn apart, and many more live in destitution and unjust squalor. The [ROOT.GetLeader] administration has made the top priority to assist the ailing populace in recovering from this tragic conflict between fellow Sichuanese.
New Sichuan's 14 Points
The New Sichuan has emerged from its decades of strife with newfound wisdom. The new progressive administration has outlined various points on how it shall approach governance of wartorn Chuan, covering economic matters, military concerns, modernisation, foreign outlook, and relations to the other provinces. Sichuan turns a new leaf today!
Modernisation through Rail and Road
In the West, impressive railroads bring interconnectedness to all regions in a nation. If China is to catch up to the might of Europe, then it must first emulate Western infrastructure. Railroads shall become the new lifeblood of the Chinese nation, and the match to set the fire shall begin here in Sichuan!
Control Arms Manufacturing
While the province-wide truce has held on for this long, a disruption in the balance of power could break the delicate house of cards. If Sichuan is to remain at peace, the minor warlords must not be allowed to acquire more weapons into their arsenals, while the Officers must maintain their military supremacy.
Standardise Troop Numbers
In an effort to outcompete one another, the various Sichuan warlords raised their armies to massive sizes at exorbitant cost. The bloated Sichuanese army has only brought about trouble for the current administration, so the Governor has declared it necessary to greatly downsize the military. Such an effort shall hopefully also curb the powers of other Sichuan warlords.
Repeal The Warlord Taxes
With many minor warlords rejecting the leaders of Chengdu and Chongqing, they could only hope to finance their tiny administrations with massive taxes upon the local populace. Such excessiveness has resulted in a spike of poverty, and [ROOT.GetLeader] shall eliminate all such taxes now that the province recognises a single polity.
Unify Provincial Currency
The various warlords in an effort to establish regionalist autonomies attempted to develop their own currency system separate from the provincial government. This has left many regions more politically divided from [ROOT.GetLeader]'s administration than expected. These regional currencies shall be removed, and the whole province shall utilise a singular monetary system.
An End to the Arbitrary
Throughout the province, abuses are commonplace. Landlords exact extortionate rent on tenants, effectively taking all harvests from the producing classes. Such barbarities shall not be tolerated in the New Sichuan, and [ROOT.GetLeader] has seen fit to establish various rent caps across all of Sichuan.
Independence of Education Funding
The previous Sichuan administration had to rely greatly upon Beijing's financial support in order to maintain various educational institutions. In events where the Central Government found itself in great turmoil, Sichuan's schools would cease to function. The province must rely on local sponsors to maintain education in the province instead.
On the Issue of Trade
In order to resuscitate the ailing Sichuanese economy, interregional trade must be restored to previous heights. The province has found itself the breadbasket of the nation, and Shu's agricultural yield shall surely bolster the financial state of the province. With the famine subsiding and our rice and grain stores restored, Sichuan's exports shall resume in full.
Limit Military Meddling
While the New Sichuanese Administration was established in part due to force of arms, the Sichuan Provincial Government shall not be operated like some Guangxi stratocracy. Civilian and military authorities must be divided, and the military must be discouraged from being used as a cudgel to enforce laws.
Create the Sichuan Central Mint
In a modern economy, financial institutions and banks have a large role to play. If enterprising businessmen find themselves in need of a loan, the Sichuan Central Mint shall give them all the money needed. This bank will be the new centre of finance in Southern China, and shall be the model of the nation hereafter!
Putting the Nail in Banditry
With much of the province in utter poverty, many have resorted to banditry to get by. These wretches have proven to be a thorn in the side of Sichuan's future stability and must be culled immediately, now that the province finally finds itself in political stability. Let it be known that Shu gives this Guangxi tradition the respect it deserves, none.
Evaluating Government Finances
If the Sichuanese Government is to embark upon a campaign to unify the Chinese nation under the Federalist flag, Xiong must ensure that Chongqing's financial position can support such a lofty goal. All previous goals of the administration must become secondary towards the new goal of National Reconstruction. While this may lead Sichuan back upon a path of war, when the ancestors call upon all Yan Huang Zisun to liberate the realm, we answer.
Taking Stock of the Military
At present, Xiong Kewu's 9 Man Regiment stands as Sichuan's strongest military force. Many of the minor warlords present meagre armies that are capable only of suppressing rowdy peasants. In the spirit of the Nation-Building Allied Army, Xiong Kewu must construct a new Federalist military out of this motley assortment of warlord forces that can stand against the major warlords of China.
Government of National Reconstruction
As more and more democrats and rump federalist federalist armies stumble into Sichuan Province, Xiong has found it prudent to call a Federalist Convention in Chongqing to establish a New Federalist Government that shall represent the cause of Free China. This new National Reconstruction Government must be able to stand against both inside and outward pressures, or Xiong's dreams shall never be realised.
Beyond the Red River Basin
For much of the Republican Era, Sichuan has found itself beset by invasions by its neighbours for opportunistic and petty gain. Our neighbours attempted to prey upon our disunity and play brother against brother. Now, it is Sichuan that stands united and ready to save all of China. While our neighbours sought to tear us apart, the National Reconstruction Government seeks only to save our fellow Chinese.
Export Militarism Avenged
After the National Protection War, the Yunnan Clique attempted to establish dominance over Sichuan after assisting us in defeating the Beiyang Clique. Under their doctrine of export militarism, the Yunnanese warlords consistently intervened beyond its borders in order to secure critical resources. It is high time Kunming was punished for its internal-imperialism and the Dian people freed from oppression.
Warpath Towards Canton
During the Warlord Era, the primary struggle could be considered one between the Beijing and Guangzhou Governments. While the Beijing Government established dominance following the fall of the Kuomintang, the lofty ideals of the Guangzhou Government live still with us. If the National Reconstruction Government could seize Guangdong, such a victory would give our government much needed legitimacy.
Descending Upon the Central Plains
The ancestral heartland of all Chinese, Zhongyuan was the birthplace of Chinese civilisation. While the Xinhai Revolution began in Wuchang, the revolution was unable to sweep across the rest of the Central Plains due to Beiyang militarist suppression. The National Reconstruction Government will see the Federalist Movement stretch further north than ever before!
The Treasures of Huadong
Eastern China has long been the economic heart of the Chinese nation. Jiangsu and Zhejiang have always been centres of trade, but the development of Shanghai during the 1800s has seen it turn into the financial centre of the East. Liberating Eastern China would allow the National Reconstruction Government to secure Shanghai finances and ensure our future military campaigns will be properly funded.
Strike North of the Great Wall
North of Beijing lies perhaps our most dangerous foe, the Fengtian Clique. Hiding behind the Great Wall and aided by the Japanese imperialists, they wield China's most industrial region and seek to extinguish any light of freedom in China. In order to destroy the taint of the Beiyang warlords forever, the Northeastern Provinces must be secured by the National Reconstruction Government.
No Preparation Too Rigorous
In our campaign to reunify China, it is likely we will come to blows with our imperialist neighbour, the Empire of Japan. For decades, Tokyo has preyed upon our ailing country, hoping to extract as many resources in the name of so-called \
To Be Inspired, Not Conquered
As we find ourselves in a War of Resistance against the Japanese invaders, let us not fall to despair. Chinese civilisation spans five thousand years of rich history, and the upstarts in Tokyo foolishly deign themselves our superiors. Let us struggle for our nation's survival against this unjust foe, let all soldiers of the Chinese military shatter the Japanese Empire here and now!
Chinese Determination, Unshaken
As this war for survival unfolds, we enter into a new type of war. This total war shall require the full energies of the Chinese masses as we struggle as one against the Japanese war machine. While Japanese morale crumbles with every mounting struggle between the two powers of East Asia, the resolve of the Chinese people only grows stronger. Victory or death against the Empire of Japan!
Lessons of the Nanchong Charter
Drafted in 1921 following months of discussion between Zhang Lan and his fellow Federalist allies, most important of which being Xiong Kewu, the Nanchong Charter was the first local piece of legislation to set forward grassroots democracy in the Sichuan basin; with many other progressive reforms in tow. We would be wise to learn from its successes, and its failures.
The Seeds of Democracy
Only a short few years ago, the Federalist Movement was confined to the trappings of Sichuan Province. Today, our National Reconstruction Government flies the Five Colour Flag in Beijing, the capital of our nation. While much of the nation has fallen into our hands, the struggle has only begun. Military unification has only brought us to the front door of reform, and now democratisation efforts must begin to take shape here in the Imperial Capital.
Local Community Politics
Chinese democracy does not begin in the centres of power in Beijing. No, it begins from the grassroots, from the village level. The most basic level of organisation across the nation, these self-governing villages led by village elders shall be the blueprint for a new Chinese democracy. Under Zhang Lan's leadership, China will finally know a government of the people, by the people, and for the people.
Compromise with the Gentry
While the Gentry have gained something of a negative reputation across China, especially amongst the lower classes, they will have a crucial role to play in the new China. China's educated have often sprung from the gentry class, and the support of the landed establishment shall keep our finances satiated. If China is to be freed, it will require proper governance spearheaded by its smartest.
Curb Provincial Vices
The disease of Opium took root in our province during the Century of Humiliation. Bringing us to the knees, this drug has all but destroyed the spirit of the Chinese people. Although opportunistic warlords have relied upon the cultivation of Opium poppies to finance their militaries, our Government must break this filth in order to be regarded as a government that stands to undo historical injustices.
The Fruits of Education
Truly, no democracy can take shape in an illiterate nation. Much of our population cannot hope to vote without the ability to read and write their opinions. Thus, education shall become paramount in our development of Chinese democracy. As the people learn Chinese values and the functions of a democratic government, citizen participation shall continually increase until our Republic stands as tall as Western powers.
Freedom of Thought and Academics
Acting as the vanguard of progressive thought in China, universities and intellectuals have often voiced their vision for Chinese political reform only to be put down by reactionary militarists. In the New China, such expression of political thought shall be encouraged, as Chinese society becomes as innovative as the days of the Chinese Golden Age!
Expand Chongqing University
In the preceding years, Chongqing has become the beating heart of Free China. As more and more intellectuals find China an increasingly hostile environment and flee to the sanctuary of the National Reconstruction Government, the Chongqing University has found itself overstaffed. Chongqing University shall reflect the new size of its staff, and lead the way for free universities across China.
Exercise in Industrial Autonomy
While much of China has stamped upon the rights of businessmen and merchants, Zhang Lan and the National Reconstruction Government hope to try a different approach. Industrialists shall be given a level of autonomy from the Federal Government in order to foster friendly business relations, but they too must follow the red lines of the President Zhang Lan or see their privileges revoked.
Integration of Labour and Learning
Truly, the Federalist Movement represents the concern of the Working Class better than anyone else. While the Beiyang warlords would crush them with an iron fist and the Kuomintang would ensnare them in their so-called National Revolution, it is the National Reconstruction Government which seeks to give them legal protections as well as education. Often illiterate, schooling for the working class would assist them in understanding and defending their rights.
Revitalise Local Enterprise
The Chinese Civil War has seen many progressive reforms both in Sichuan and other provinces disrupted by armed conflict and chaos. The National Reconstruction Government, not content to reign over a nation of dust and ash, has seen to it that businesses and enterprises in war-torn regions and rural hinterland be supported, and hopefully begin to recover even while other provinces continue to engage in high level fighting.
The Professional Associations System
As proposed by Zhang Junmai of the Democratic Socialist Party, the National Reconstruction Government ought to represent Chinese people of all classes. Critical professions to national interests must be supported, and associations formed to organise them. Through these organisations, the Federal Government and these classes can collaborate for mutual benefit.
Abolish Tax Pre-Collection
Tax Pre-Collection is a policy that allows lenders to prematurely close accounts from borrowers who are unexpected to pay off their debt, and see their debt sold to a collection agency. A predatory policy that harms the working class of China, this abominable practice will be excised from China's shores, hopefully never to return.
A New Unified Currency
With political divides in China lasting decades, the various rival governments have begun to issue differing currency in their respective borders. With many of these governments militarily defeated by the Federal Military, it has left the President with the mess of sorting through these various currencies. With support from the National Assembly, President [ROOT.GetLeader] has offered the people of China to hand in their invalid currencies to exchange with our currency.
Rally the Intelligentsia
With various intellectuals finding themselves in Sichuan, frictions have emerged between the fractious groups. Zhang Junmai has continually attempted to assert himself as a leading force in the Federal Government, and a splintering of lines between the Grand Republican Alliance and China Democratic League has left many disgruntled. However, if our movement is to survive, we must continue to sustain the unity of the early government which brought us success.
Creating a Provisional Capital
With more and more of China's major cities falling to the military forces of the Federal Republic, it has become more pressing to establish a better Provisional Capital for our National Reconstruction Government. Chongqing, having served its purpose, is not necessarily the best place from which to govern the newly conquered provinces, and while Beijing is the traditional centre of government, some believe a change is needed.
Combatting the Root of Apathy
When the Republic of China was first established, a rush of idealism struck the nation. However, years of warlord fighting and foreign exploitation has left the spirit of the Chinese people woefully apathetic to political changes. If a democracy is to take root in the Middle Kingdom, economic and political reforms must be undertaken to jolt the Chinese people out of passivity.
Overtures to Student Radicals
With the allure of socialism has become more and more attractive to idealistic student groups, there has been a growing number of radical student groups operating from the major universities within the National Reconstruction Government. Protesting working conditions, these groups demand the government do more. Perhaps hoping to turn them into a pillar of support, President [ROOT.GetLeader] has offered some concessions to these groups and a United Front.
Agreements with the YCP
A titanic mass movement entrenched in Sichuan and the Central Plains, the Young China Party is a nationalist force spread across military and intellectual circles. Although the fall of the Zhili Clique has crippled their movement, they remain a viable force in mass party politics. Well acquainted with their leadership, President [ROOT.GetLeader] has invited them to the government.
Promoting Harmonious Bipartisanship
Although the election certainly saw tensions between the China Democratic League and Grand Republican Alliance flare, President Dan hopes to repair tensions between Xiong Kewu and Zhang Lan. While the China Democratic League is the main opposition party, both the GRA and CDL do hope for largely the same vision for China, and collaboration between the two parties will surely be in China's interest.
The Safeguard against Autocracy
While the military has traditionally been a force for warlordism, the Federal military stands unique across all Chinese armies. The Jianguojun, like the political leadership of the National Reconstruction Government, fights for the democratic cause, and can be trusted to intervene if the President ever slips into tyranny. The people of China can rest easy knowing that even if the government forgets its commitments to democracy, Liu Wenhui will not.
Building a Fair Cabinet
As our National Reconstruction Government incorporates more territories and parties, it is only fair that our administration evolves along with the nation. In order to maintain the unity that saw the Federal Government rise to become the main government of China, the President's cabinet shall include representation from the major parties participating in the government, as well as qualified technocrats from professional associations.
Parameters of the Legislature
In a functioning republic, the legislature must take primacy above the Presidential Executive. The Federal Parliament's powers and responsibilities shall be clearly outlined, and it shall be divided into two bodies, the House of Representatives and the Senate. Each house shall have a speaker and deputy speaker elected by its members, and terms shall be set by the Constitution. May this body govern the people well!
Reviving the Chinese Democratic Process
While China has never officially strayed from democracy after 1912, it was rendered largely out of the equation following the cancellation of elections in 1933. As our Government of National Reconstruction marches forward, President [ROOT.GetLeader] strives to revive these antiquated institutions which were so frequently abused, and improve upon the minuscule reforms made by the Beiyang warlords.
Increase Troop Funding
If the National Reconstruction Government hopes to lead unification of the Chinese nation, we must see to it that the army is sufficiently bolstered. While the Jianguojun still exhibits a concerning level of warlordism and factionalism, President Zhang and Premier Xiong have no choice but to embark on this course of action, or the Federal Movement will die in Sichuan.
Recruiting Sympathetic Officers
While Yang Sen, Liu Cunhou, and Liu Xiang were opportunistic warlords who fought for their own petty interests, a small number of their subordinates either rose up due to meritorious service or were sympathetic to our cause. These officers may help form a new loyalist bloc within the Jianguojun, and help root out particularly egregious warlords within our ranks.
Reach out to the Baoding Department
As the Baoding Department was not aligned with the Officers or 9 Man Regiment when Yang Sen and Liu Xiang fell from power, the triumvirate suffered a major setback in power from Xiong's elevation to the Governorship. Liu Wenhui for his part has already opted to support Xiong, but Deng Xihou and Tian Songyao have remained both out of government and out of power. Due to Liu's prodding, Xiong has reluctantly invited the other Baoding warlords to the table.
Renovate Arsenal Capacities
While minor arsenals have allowed Sichuanese warlords to remain a regional power in China, they are not sufficient for the National Reconstruction Government to launch a military campaign for total reunification. No, Sichuan's minor military arsenals must be improved upon substantially in order to feed the Federalist Jianguojun's war effort in the coming Chinese Civil War.
Root Out Incompetence and Ineptitude
As the Jianguojun's initial ranks encompass all warlord forces within the province, the quality of the Federalist military is unenviably inconsistent. While Xiong's personal forces rank as the army's elite, minor warlords that have operated more like bandits are barely equipped and untrained for real warfare. If the Jianguojun is to become a real force, Xiong must see to it that unskilled bandits and corrupt officers are removed and replaced with meritorious replacements.
An Era Illuminated by Sacrifice
In this time of chaos, heroes and villains have risen and fallen as circumstances change. The great Cai E fought to depose the autocrat Yuan Shikai's imperial regime, even as his own health faded away. Many more have followed in his example, truly heroes in the image of Liu Bei and Zhuge Liang. If the Federalist Democratic Revolution is to succeed, many more sacrifices will likely be made on the path to unification, and the Republic will honour them all when the dust settles.
Restoring Naval Projection
During the Ming Dynasty, China sported the greatest navy in the world. The Late Qing attempted to emulate Ming successes as well as modern innovations through the Beiyang Navy, but it met an ill-fated end when faced against the Imperial Japanese Navy. With our National Reconstruction Government ascendant, it falls upon us to restore Chinese pride on the seas, and once again dominate the waters of Asia.
Soaring in Free Skies
As the modern age of warfare progresses, it has become apparent that the airforce shall play an integral role. The Federal Government previously relied on pure infantry forces in order in its military unification campaigns, but as our government begins to fight more modern forces in Northern China and neighbouring powers, developing a modern airforce has become paramount to the Federalist war effort.
The Last Bastion of Federalism
While Sichuan was still in the midst of civil war, the provinces of Zhejiang and Hunan had already promulgated their own provincial constitutions. However, in a cruel twist of irony, it seems that Sichuan has emerged from its civil war only to find all other Federalist provinces in the thrall of tyrants. Now Xiong Kewu stands as the final leading federalist, and he will not squander his moment on the national stage.
The Vibrant Bipartisan Democracy
While Zhang Lan was the face of our National Reconstruction Government during the Chinese Civil War, it was Xiong Kewu and Dan Maoxin who led the Jianguojun to ultimate victory. Recognised as the swords of liberty, the Chinese people have resoundingly backed Dan Maoxin and Xiong Kewu to be the new leaders of our Federal Republic. While the CDL has emerged as our political rivals, we welcome this as a sign of a burgeoning bipartisan republic.
A Forum for the Level-headed
Chinese Governance has long seen itself abused by personalism, idealogues, and demagoguery; those tokens of the irrational and intolerable. But a healthy democracy must let itself be lead by debate and discussion; words and law over rifle and shell. To this end, the government must enforce fair compliance in the organs of the Republic, so as to enable true Republicanism to flourish.
Enshrine Provincial Constitutions
The Local Self-Governance project sought to rectify China's national problems of inefficiency, and inability to rule its large domain. By taking the merits of the system of the United States, or of Germany, it would see itself free of the litany of problems of despotism at its political centre. Accommodating for the role of the Central Government, let us enshrine the province as the building block of the new China.
Encourage Local Initiative
Any form of centrally planned economic management is sure to wound up in disaster; and beyond the grand aspirations for socialism, or utopia, the nation itself still remains largely feudal in various areas. To enable further economic development in this time of great healing, the government shall provide for local entrepreneurial endeavours. For salvation of the nation may only emerge through industrialisation.
Participation Across Class
Radicals within the opposition would see it so that China tears itself apart in some sort of mythical class struggle, bound to rebuild itself upon a National Revolution, or through insidious reformist socialism. They would fail to see that China's greatest strength is that of common brotherhood, in working towards a grand harmonious arrangement; between gentry and peasant, worker and official, civilian and soldier.
National Demobilisation
The Warlord Era's profane enabling of local military commanders to both amass significant wealth and a disparate band of soldiers has contributed greatly to the nation's inability to reject foreign imperialism, or otherwise recover since the Xinhai Revolution. Whilst Wu Peifu attempted National Demobilisation and failed, the new Republic carries with it a vigour that is utterly unrelenting in the persecution of warlordism.
Cooperate With Regional Notables
The government cannot hope to enforce its will upon all citizenry in equal standing, and thus it is in desperate need of local allies. Men who, having committed no clear acts of treason, could be solicited to provide local outreach efforts within regions that otherwise remain aloof of the Capital. Be they local peasant leader, gentry, or businessman, all must come together for the betterment of the nation.
The Great Beiyang Reapproachement
The opposition would see to it that a great array of skilled bureaucrats, politicians, and magistrates be cast aside for they are \
Depoliticise the Ranks
Politics and personnel waltzing hand-in-hand has resulted in some of the nation's most recent tragedies. The machinations of Yuan Shikai, the despotism of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and his National Revolutionary Army, or that of the Zhili, Fengtian, or Anhui. The army is not the path for careerism and self-actualisation of idealogical goals, but for that of duty, honour, and service.
Bicameral Democracy Realised
China's Democracy, its previous attempts, that is, have long held themselves to the ideals built upon a bicameral legislature: the Assembly, and the Senate. With the latter having acting powers to effectively check both the cabinet and the Assembly, it has proven itself utterly incapable. With a renewed martial legalism in government, the very institutions of the Republic have received newfound primacy.
From Resistance to Reconstruction
Against all odds Zhang Lan has secured electoral victory, thwarting upstarts within the China Democratic League and handily defeating Dan Maoxin's Grand Republican Alliance. Considered a radical by reactionary elements, President Zhang finds opposition from many elements of Chinese society. An idealistic socialist with a heart of gold, President Zhang stands ready to enact his ambitious and radical plan for reconstructing the Chinese Republic, one reform at a time.
The Wisdom of West and East
While the West has certainly achieved levels of modernisation China ought to emulate, we must avoid shunning our own past. Our path to the modern world will certainly be unique to China, and we must strive to balance what we learn from the West with our own culture. China was once the greatest empire in the world, and in combining the lessons of the past and those of the present, we may reach for the skies.
Mobilising the Broadest Masses
While the Intellectual class of China have historically been the vanguard of Chinese culture and political development, we must not forget the agrarian masses. Throughout Chinese history, the peasantry have toiled under arbitrary warlords and tyrannical emperors, and the President empathises with their struggle. No longer shall society's betters oppress the nation's bedrock, for we are only as great as our poorest social classes.
The Gathering Of Many Minds
An important trait to a stable democracy is learning to rule through consensus. As such, President Zhang Lan has called a conference of China's most prestigious and respected intellectuals to advise him on vital policy matters, even inviting his political rival Zhang Junmai to participate in the name of easing tensions. In bringing together many bright minds, the President is confident that many solutions to China's most pressing concerns shall be put forward.
Form Substance And Spirit
A common criticism of Zhang Lan and other progressive intellectuals is that they lack understanding of the common folk and provide no practical solutions to economic and social problems beyond a vague call for further democratic reform. Fully aware of his critics, President Zhang Lan plans on demonstrating to the people the practicality of his national reconstruction plan through meaningful economic development and financial stabilisation.
Rebirth Of The Political Animal
After the Republic was declared, the intellectual classes hoped to represent the nation as its leading political class. However, Chinese intellectuals would find warlords and militarists sitting on the Republican throne. Forced to compromise under such circumstances, the civilian political class would find difficulty in pushing meaningful reform. With the military no longer the guiding hand of the Republic, the civilian political class may finally bring change through the pen.
Professionalize The Soldierly Class
While the Jianguojun was instrumental in bringing about the new Federal Republic, we must acknowledge it to be a desperate assortment of Sichuan's various warlords. With the nation finally at peace, the Chinese military must be restructured to make it into a proper military force, rather than a bloated mess of provincial forces and bandits. While Xiong Kewu and his allies may grumble, the new Republic is not guided by the blade.
Rein In Army Cliques
Throughout the Republic's history, military cliques have traditionally been a leading force in influencing the nation's political direction either through the sword or behind closed doors. Hoping to put such undemocratic circles in China's past, President Zhang Lan plans to take on these military factions directly and see them eliminated once and for all. Let it be known that anti-democratic behaviour will no longer be tolerated!
Nationwide Industrial Autonomy
In a country as large as China, it would be absurd to expect the Central Government to properly accommodate regions to their economic needs efficiently. President Zhang Lan has instead opted to allow the provinces to loosen their reins on economic policy, so that local businesses may thrive without unnecessary oversight. A nation that develops naturally is a nation that develops healthily.
Democracy As The Key
Our Republic was not always dominated by military strongmen. During the dream of 1912, the people of China eagerly participated in the first free election in the nation's history. However, Song Jiaoren's assassination would turn our dream into an unending nightmare, with warlords supplanting warlords day after day. Now, President Zhang Lan has finally wrangled the beast of militarism back into its cage, and the Republic may finally live up to the Dream of 1912.
Leading By Word and Deed
Chinese democracy is a fickle thing; few can seem to truly master it, lest it succumb to its own torturous ideology. The time for ruling by legalism and pretty speeches has past; it is time for China's true saviours to lead her to modernity and salvation. Without quarter, Civil Governance will be restored, and Progress shall be achieved.
Society's Proper Placements
Once former politicians and warlords have nothing to do, they will simply stir up trouble in society, criticise this and that and obstruct government order. But once given work in productive developments, even if it's just a small responsibility, their disruptive influence will be greatly reduced. Let every Chinese citizen know their proper place in a productive society, one ruled by modernity, and not ideology.
Legacy Of The Academy
The Baoding Military Academy is perhaps China's greatest military institution. Having tutored some of the nation's greatest strategists and tacticians, it is a prized institution that has been treated utterly unfairly for its stature. The glories of its alumni are many, and through additional funding directed at Baoding, it may but achieve even greater heights in future wars.
Enshrine Military Primogeniture
China's military is both its greatest enemy, and its strongest vanguard. Whilst a crippling weakness if not properly parleyed with, the nation is in the hands of its strongest military forces; and thus their rights must be assured and protected. Whilst President Liu may be disgruntled at the notion of pervasive military influence in civilian governance, it is the nature of the beast that he has saddled himself with.
A Use For All
By funding training programs to prepare the unemployed for technical roles, the nation can both slash its unemployed population, alongside creating a new caste of directors and specialists. They benefit from employment, training, a fulfilling job, and a secure livelihood, and the government benefits from their support. The days of the drifting layabout are over! Thus arrives the new productive society!
The Push for Efficiency
Chinese governance has long sought to enrich its benefactors through flagrant abuses of taxation, and of bureaucracy. By merging redundant departments, eliminating government agencies deemed to be useless, and the filtering of capital from useless places to areas that desperately need the funding, China's industrialisation will accelerate in unbridled ferocity.
Western Revitalisation Plan
Xikang and Sichuan where but mere backwaters; mountains, and rugged terrain. Yet, through the skilled development programs of Liu Wenhui, Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, and all others of the Baoding Department, they have grown into industrial powerhouses! China's Northwest is but a vast cornucopia of potential, and the Chinese citizens must but be properly incentivised to venture and seize their own destinies!
Overcoming Internal Backwardness
Chinese internal competition and divisions has long led to a situation of muddled feudalistic development and dirty self-serving capitalism. No longer! China will progress, even if it must drag ever gentryman and businessman by their heels! Only through self-sacrifice, endurance, vigour, and spirit shall we persevere! Chinese potential abounds, and every citizen must work towards the betterment of the country!
Streamline County Magistrates
The current array of national magistrates and low-level officials have shown their true colours with recent developments within national politics. Instead choosing loyalty towards the disloyal and perfidious, they have refused tacitly, or otherwise protested, the current government. Such blatant inefficiencies cannot be tolerated, and it is imperative that the government forcefully streamline internal administrations - to its own ends.
A Nation not only of Critics
There is no time for idealist dribble! The nation must be developed industrially! The masses are hungry, they lack productive employment, they lack even the money to sufficiently clothe themselves. The nation needs workers and producing classes, not intellectuals and critics of the downtrodden nation. Whatever avenues for dialogue are present, they can wait until the nation is even capable of standing on its own two feet.
Modernity's Five Spirits
The Five Spirits, that of Science, that of Endurance, of Aspiration, of Loyalty and Public Duty, and of Research, are the keys to which every nation achieves true Modernity. Britain, France, Russia, Germany, the United States, and even Japan, have all retained these spiritual guides on the path to greatness; and China must follow suite. Through systematic development, the next century may very well be the Chinese one.
To Seek Prosperity
Money is the root of all evil, as they say, but the government must work to dismiss the social attitude that money is intrinsically linked to petty warlords, conniving businessmen, and crooked officials! Every citizen must know their avenues to progress and better their lives, they must hoist that of the upright and effective administrators!
New Style Education
Education must be of that for the everyman; it must serve as a baseline for life itself. Thus, the government must place due prioritisation of financing the Ministry of Education, and draw out within the Chinese youth their own potential for future generations. Those ivory tower intellectuals yearn to prioritise the universities, but how can a university function without fundamental education before it?
A Reliable National Constabulary
The last few decades of Chinese societal experiences have proven themselves to be evident in one thing: when the nation experiences disorder, bandits, petty criminals, and thieves run amok. And with the military predisposed towards national defence rather than internal policing, there is but one solution. Following the lead of cadets educated in America under August Vollmer, China must revolutionise its policing.
True Purposes of Knowledge
Knowledge is the key to any nation's success, and to one's own personal success. It can be utilised for any means; to achieve power, to achieve change, or to achieve success. With altruistic applications and self-servicing ones, those with the most knowledge reign supreme over those without; thus the question is raised, what is the true purpose of knowledge? For higher office and political power? Or the advancement of China?
To Cultivate Talent
Talent is by and large one of the most crucial facets of national development, for without talent there is no culture, there is no innovation, and there is very little progress. And without noticing, or enabling, such talent, the nation is within a complete dearth of talent in the first place. Through intensified schooling efforts, and scholarly grants, China shall enable its best and brightest to truly succeed.
Specialised Practical Schools
Without a shadow of a doubt, schools must be revolutionised across the nation. Furthermore, even more schools must be opened in all places; for no child within the nation should have to traverse life without experiencing the liberating light of education. By incentivising schools focused on practical skillsets, the nation will experience both an influx of workers, and their own self-enlightenment.
Appeal to the Disenfranchised
China is a nation of many creeds and many backgrounds. Yet it is overwhelmingly dominated by the upper echelons: the rich, the elite, the wealthy, and the powerful. Those without power have commonly found themselves beholden to local folk heroes: Lu Rongting, Chen Quzhen, Long Yun. The government cannot allow the disenfranchised within China to feel further isolated from their nation-state, and it must work to integrate them further.
Develop the Industrial Stepstones
The nation cannot be industrialised without first achieving the proper stepping stones unto its own prosperity; through owning its own resources, and by providing for its own masses, the nation's industrialisation is all but guaranteed. Alongside implementing workers' protections and new workers' laws, China shall adjourn even the revolutionary states on the moral of its productive classes.
The Zhili's Last Stand
Despite the Royalist's rather foolish attempt to decapitate our Clique by murdering Cao Kun and Wu Peifu in cold blood, they would underestimate our Clique's capacity to rise from the ashes like a mighty phoenix. Rallying under the auspices of the Marshal of Tianjin, and with the most grateful assistance of our true comrades Yang Sen and Liu Cunhou, we will transform Sichuan into the foundational base camp to annihilate the Emperor.
Modernisation of the Desperate
The task before us of taking on the traitors that exiled us is a gargantuan one. If we are to take on the Qing, Sichuan's war-torn industrial base won't do. We'll need to double our industrial efforts, utilise ever resource we can possibly possess in its most absolute form, and dedicate the full strength of the Zhili Clique. All for our final reclamation.
Partners of Law and Order
Germany has long been an erstwhile friend of the Zhili in the past, even if temporarily estranged as of recent years. Without them, the Zhili Clique may very well have seen its extinction in the late 1920s. Through our connections and ties to the AOG, the Legation Cities and German East Asia, we're in a position to bring in engineers from Krupp to assist us in the construction of new weapon facilities under this German supervision.
Emulating the Smiling Tiger
Whilst much detested in Northern Zhili Circles, it would appear, despite the state of his League, that Sun Chuanfang was indeed correct about something. With our ties to Germany restored and business flourishing, we'll be able to import as many German guns as our gold reserves can purchase. With German armaments, we are sure to annihilate the under-equipped Royalist soldiers.

With President Yan having descended from the famous and adored Diplomatic Corps, he has seen it fit to welcome Diplomat Wellington Koo into our government. New Leaf of a Reborn Republic
No more shall the Beiyang Republic be ruled by military strongmen! No more shall the legacy of Xinhai be beholden to autocrats! The mission of Good People's Governance shall be seen to fruition, and by welcoming the participation of the Political Science Clique and the Independents, we shall construct a true Assembly and Senate that answers to the people.
Three Cliques, One Mission
Our administrative structure is a horrific and hastily composed abomination of the Armament Department's local provincial administration, and the influx of both Beiyang and Zhili officials. Rather unfortunately brought together in such dire circumstances, the Armament Department, the Jinbao Clique and the Luoyang Clique must ultimately streamline and unify their internal structures, so as to ensure efficient governance.
Legacy of Jinbao and Luoyang
The most premier of any and all warlord cliques, the Jinbao and Luoyang factions of the Zhili Clique are perhaps the closest Cliques to completing the full transition to good, responsible statesmen. With many members of either faction having folden within the civilian bureaucracy, we have truly proven the fact that the Zhili are the legitimate rulers of China. Orthodox and principled, technocratic governance is assured under our watch.

To modernise and surpass our forebears, whilst preserving their intentions, we must follow precisely in Cao Kun's footsteps. Drafting our own constitution, considering the faults and merits of the previous, we will march into a new era of liberty and prosperity.

Shu's March of Progress

Together, hand-in-hand, a new China is forged.
March of the Grieving Army
True, our army grieves. For it has lost not only its leader, but one of its greatest commanders. As much as the animosity between Marshal Wang and Marshal Wu tore them apart, at the end of the day they still had a duty to do. Wu served to the end, fulfilling his duty. No doubt attempting to defend Cao from hails of bullets. Similarly, Marshal Wang and the rest of the Zhili Army must march forever onwards. For their memory, at the very least.
The Return of Tianjin
Finally, the odd one out, the little Clique in the internal Zhili power struggle, Tianjin has formally succeeded both Baoding and Luoyang. Whilst it was merged into that of Baoding to form Jinbao, it nonetheless has survived both Cao and Wu. With its founders being that of the late Cao Rui, Bian Shoujing and of course, Marshal Wang, Tianjin used to play second fiddle to Wu and Cao. Not any more.
Constitutionalism for the Masses
Cao Kun's service and sacrifice will not be forgotten. He may have been murdered along with Wu, but his legacy will live on through the constitution he drafted in 1923. A hallmark piece of legislature, it will provide the people with the security and freedoms they deserve, both here in Sichuan as well as Beijing when we return home. Truly without Cao Kun, there would be no new China.
Government of One Mind, One Body
For too long has the meddling assembly bickered over the intricacies of legislature, the whims of bureaucrats derailing good governance for their ill-informed agendas. Their damnable haranguing nearly cost the whole Zhili Clique, and their prized Beiyang Democracy! For this period of reclamation, the governmental body must act with one mindset, and in perfect unison. Surely even our opposition will adhere to such a fact.
Government of Bread and Circuses
Despite our best efforts, there are still those that do not understand their place by putting personal interests ahead of the nation. For these individuals we must appease them during this time of great struggle. Satisfying the people's most immediate requirements and desires, they may support our regime for its perennial struggle. Reform will happen, but it must wait until the reconquest.
Primacy of the Central Army
To best face the challenges that lie ahead our society will need be a militant one. From top to bottom, we'll embrace the virtues of military service and honour the Central Army. For without the Central Army, the legacy of Xinhai would very much have died in the coup. Knowing this, our soldiers will be instilled with a greater sense of duty and valour, putting them well above the rabble our enemy is sure to field.
Salvaging the Lessons of Baoding
We may have been deposed from the most premier of all military academies within the nation, but its lessons stay with us no matter where we travel. By refining local training methods on the merits of Baoding, we'll have our officers and soldiers drilled to a point where they'll be better equipped not only to adapt to battlefield developments, but we'll be more resilient to any loss of institutional knowledge.
The Nation's First Line of Defence
We must always be three steps ahead of our enemies. By giving more freedom to our military intelligence branch to act unrestrained, we'll know every move our enemy makes, be it a foreign or internal threat. One of our many follies was not adequately trusting our military intelligence rings before it was too late. Marshal Wang shall not make such a mistake. The people of China will forever be safe under the Public Safety Bureau.
Prepare The Final Offensive
Sichuan province is rapidly preparing itself for the twilight struggle. For the final push. Our entire society backs both Military and Marshal. With the will of the people in earnest, nothing shall prevent us from marching forward to reclaim what was rightfully our's. The fools thought they had ended the Zhili Clique by brutally executing the Jade Marshal and King of Baoding. They were utterly wrong.
Homecoming of Vengeance
Hate. Hate and revenge. That is what fuels the Marshal most presently. Together with the civilians, the remnants of Beiyang, and his ever loyal Zhili officers and soldiers, the Zhili Clique shall bring the much anticipated hammer to the anvil. A true testament to our resilience and preparation of the past months. To fail is an impossibility! This is not just for our forebears, but for the very essence of China itself!
Xinhai All Over Again!
We rose from the ashes after the Qing thought they'd destroyed us. Now they and everyone else that stood with them against us have been humbled by our victories. We must consolidate our position and restore order to China, for the Zhili is here to stay. The restoration of normal efforts in the Assembly, collaboration with the Senate, and widely anticipated elections has resulted in a new burst of idealism.
Elections of the Victorious
Most fortuitously, Marshal Wang and Diplomat Yan were truly only leaders in the nation's most dire moments. With the restoration of our rightful place within the Chinese nation, a series of scheduled national elections have been announced. The first to have been held in many years. Hopefully with the new mandate, the new president can foresee a period of reconciliation, reconstruction, and new popular support.
Unity Forged Through Tragedy
Surrounded by the rubble, the bodies of our comrades, the tears of the revolutionaries, and the ashes of the nation. It is hard to be patriotic for the Chinese nation at this stage. Yet with our shared suffering, a mutual bond is built. Forged to be unbreakable. Our struggle may be over, but out nation still labours. Together however, we march forward unto a new horizon.
Reconstitute the Beiyang Navy
Once the pride of the nation, the Beiyang Navy used to dominate the Asian seas and protect China's coastline. Now it is nothing more than a shadow, neglected by the government. To truly reclaim the birthright of the Chinese Republic, we similarly must revive China's naval tradition. Famously apolitical, mostly, the Navy worked with the Manchus, however we cannot blame them. After all, they only want to sail the seas.
Forging Modernity through Strength
Whilst they rather reluctantly collaborated with the Manchu Royalists, it has become increasingly clear that the Young China Party were merely victims of their own hubris. For of course their pursuit for national prominence clouded their capacity for nationalist republicanism. Coming to us with their tail between their legs, the YCP will prove themselves useful partners for the new modern China!
Idealism Revisited in Wu's Name
The intellectuals in Beijing are both our greatest boon and worst enemy. They continue to champion their agitation for decades, and evidently are not diseappearing anytime soon. Yet some intellectuals such as Hu Shih and Bai Jianwu were imperative in our reconquest, and in the sustenance of the Zhili Clique. Let us approach these brave idealists, in the name of the Jade Marshal's noble mission for a democratic Confucian Republic.
Five Races Under One Union Forever-more!
The age of warlords and self-serving tyrants needs to come to an end! Through national unification the Beiyang Republic has seen its reconstitution and revival following the tenuous decades of the 1910s and 1920s. Rallying not just the Zhili, but the intellectuals, republicans and democrats too, we shall make a new united China, together.
All Under the Auspicious Cloud
Considered to be a token of good faith and good luck, all of the domain of China as dignified by the Republic of 1911's borders must be brought under our goodwill. With our border regions frequently contested between our rightful kinsmen and foreign imperialists, this is surely a difficult and titanic task. But if we are to bring enlightenment to the whole of China, we must control the whole of China.

Expand the Jinghan Railroad

The §aSichuan Clique§! in 1936
As 1936 dawns, §aSichuan§! remains in a very fragile balance between its multiple factions. §aYang Sen§! holds for now, buoyed by §PZhili§! support from his personal backer, the §PJade Marshal Wu Peifu§! and aided by his close associate and former governor of §aSichuan§!, §PLiu Cunhou§!, whose status and connections, as well as considerable forces, give §aYang§! sorely needed stability and legitimacy. The §aSichuan Clique§!
The modern history of §aSichuan§! begins in 1912. When the §lXinhai Revolution§! reached §aSichuan§!, the region entered a period of prolonged instability, with regional warlords vying for the governorship by diplomacy and force. Between 1912 and 1926, the region was alternatively controlled by §lXinhai revolutionaries§!, §RKuomintang loyalists§! and §Plocal warlords§!.\n\nThis state of affairs would last until the failure of the Northern Expedition in 1926. With the personal support of the victorious §PZhili§! leader, §cWu Peifu§!, §aYang Sen§! was able to establish himself as the firm ruler of §aSichuan§!, finally restoring some semblance of stability to the region. However, the profound divisions within §aSichuan would§! not disappear, with §aYang§! rapidly becoming beheld to the interests for various internal cliques that formed and unable to remove their influence. §PLiu Xiang§!, one of these warlords, established himself in §PChongqing§! by allying himself with the local administration, quickly becoming §aYang's§! main rival for control over §aSichuan§!.\n\n1928 saw §aSichuan§! face an invasion from the neighbouring clique of §aYunnan§!. While at first a success, the invasion was soon defeated by §aSichuanese§! forces, causing considerable losses among §aYang's§! personal forces. A §PTibetan§! invasion in 1930 deteriorated the situation even further, with §PTibetan§! troops reaching the Yangtze River and directly threatening the capital of §aChengdu§!. While the involvement of the §PMa Clique§! to the north eventually turned the tide against the §PTibetans§!, §aSichuan§! was forced to cede half of the §aXikang§! region to §PTibet§! and §aYang's§! military was left in tatters.
The §aSichuan Clique§! (Part 2)
While the §PTibetan§! invasion was repelled, this was not the end of §aSichuan's§! troubles. In 1931, a group of §RKuomintang-aligned§! officers, §Pwarlords§! and §aformer governors§! of §aSichuan§!, the §SOfficer Department§!, launched its first expedition into §aSichuan§! from their bases in northern §aYunnan§!, with tacit support from §PTang Jiyao's Republican government§!. The tattered §aSichuanese§! forces under §aYang§! were no match for the §RKMT§! troops, being routed time and again, losing most of their supplies to the advancing invasion forces. With the §aClique§! on the brink of collapse, warlord §aYang Sen§!, in a move of desperation, formed a temporary alliance with §PChongqing§! warlord §PLiu Xiang§! and his clique, the §PIndustrial Corps§!. With assistance from §PLiu's§! forces, §aYang§! was able to beat back the expedition. Further cooperation with the §PIndustrial Corps§! allowed §aSichuan§! to begin rebuilding its army, at the cost of ever increasing §PIndustrial Corps§! influence within the government.\n\nAnother group to rise in influence at this time was §cDeng Xihou's Baoding Department§!, whose forces helped suppress the §SOfficer Department§! while §aYang§! rebuilt his forces. The highly visible work by the §cBaoding Department§! in suppressing the rebels led to an increase in the group's popularity, which is seen by more and more citizens as the true protectors of §aSichuan§!.\n\nAnother invasion attempt in 1933 by §aYunnan§!, in support of the §SOfficer Department§!, was quickly aborted when the §PLeague-Marshal of the Eight Provinces§!, §PSun Chuanfang§!, threatened to intervene. The unexpected §aYunnanese§! retreat allowed §aYang§! to partially reoccupy §asouthern Sichuan§!. The chaos also allowed §aTian Songyao§! to establish himself in the northeast as a §aminor warlord§!, yet his ambitions remain a mystery.
§aSichuan§!, Divided
§aSichuan§! in 1936 stands divided, with multiple factions vying for absolute power.\n\nThe ruling faction at the moment is the §aArmament Department§!, led by §aYang Sen§! and his close associate §PLiu Cunhou§!. Due to §cWu Peifu's§! personal support over the years, the §aDepartment§! is closely aligned to the §PZhili authorities§! in §cBeijing§! and §PNanjing§!. Should the opportunity appear, the §PIndustrial Corps§! may quickly reconsider the usefulness of their alliance with §aYang Sen§!.\n\nThe third most important faction is the §cBaoding Department§!, a clique formed by former §cBaoding§! graduates - though this is not a prerequisite for membership - and led by §aYang's§! general §cDeng Xihou§!. Unrest in the South
Following the sale of the ZheGan railroad in the League of Eight Provinces, worrying rumours of widespread unrest have begun to emerge. Starting off as whispers of protests suppressed by League police forces, our border guards now report streams of refugees fleeing violence and an explosion of banditry flowing across our borders.\n\nIt appears a peaceful protest in Wuhu escalated into a violent bloodbath after League forces fired upon the protestors - a scene that began to repeat itself across the League in the days following what is now being termed the 'Wuhu Incident'. Some are now claiming the League - and the Zhili order that backs it up - are on their last legs, though most are still willing to believe that military force can keep the unrest contained.
It will pass, as it has done in the past.
Marshal Sun Chuanfang Shot by Assassin
Grave news coming from the League of Eight Provinces: League-Marshal Sun Chuanfang, the highest Zhili authority in the region, lays in a coma, mortally wounded after being shot by an assassin. Zhili control over the south has already begun to break down and it will not be long before the waves reach us in Sichuan. Should the worst come and the south fall to chaos, Beijing may become too busy to be able to assist us.
This doesn't bode well.
Chaos in the South
Our worst nightmares have become reality. Zhili control over Southern China has completely broken down. In Nanjing, general Qi Xieyuan has appointed himself acting League-Marshal after assuming control of the city. With the League collapsing in the aftermath of Sun's shooting, KMT rebels long thought suppressed have risen up in Fujian in an attempt to restore the National Government. The governor of Anqing has declared war on Qi, accusing him of masterminding the assassination attempt to take over the League. Further west, the governors of Hunan, Guangxi and Guangdong have refused to recognise the authority of the new League-Marshal, but so far have not opened hostilities.\n\nThe situation has become dire enough for the central government in Beijing to become directly involved, with Qing troops and supplies already on their way south. For now, it seems Beijing's attention is completely captured by the crisis to the south and we are on our own.

Dissidents all over China are already loudly proclaiming Wu's decision as proof of Zhili weakness and incompetence. It seems Zhili control over China is breaking and our enemies are surely watching.
This is a catastrophe!
Liu Xiang Mobilises Against Us
As the fragile Sichuanese order turns against us with the troubles in the League of Eight Provinces, Liu Xiang has decided to cross the Rubicon, so to speak. With his large army, he has moved out of Chongqing and soldiers loyal to him have been seen moving all around Sichuan, mainly in its Eastern portions. Our former allies have betrayed us and our friends have left us. For now, however, the Baoding Department has decided to maintain the course. All around Sichuan, armies are mobilising - and we must mobilise too. The time has come for us to cast the die, the fate of Sichuan hangs in the balance.
We must stop him!
Sichuan Collapses into Civil War
Sichuan has descended into chaos.\n\nAll across the province, the forces of the formally allied Accelerated Department battle with one another, with Liu Xiang's forces battling Yang Sen's forces. The Armament Department and the Baoding Department have temporarily allied with Yang Sen's forces, and have been joined by the minor Officer Department, fighting side-by-side against the largest army in Sichuan. Liu Xiang has continued to issue offensive orders from his command in Chongqing for his troops to move in and engage all forces of the Yang Sen Accelerated Department, Armament Department, and Baoding Department.\n\nIn Tongren, the federalist forces under Xiong Kewu have seen an opportunity to make their way back into Sichuan. Joined by the remnant Kuomintang forces under Lü Chao, and the ever present guerrillas in South-Eastern Sichuan, they have proven themselves capable of knocking the delicate Sichuan order into complete disarray.\n\nThe Baoding Department has, so far, remained loyal to Chengdu, with their forces fighting alongside Yang Sen's in the bloody war of provincial unification. The facade of stability in Sichuan has been broken and only the heavens know what will come of the province.
Contact Beijing at once, we need their aid!
So it begins...
Accelerated Department Seeks Asylum
The civil war in Sichuan has ended, and our allies in the Accelerated Department and the Armament Deprtment have been defeated by their enemies. Fleeing possible retribution, the leadership of the former ruling clique of Sichuan have arrived, seeking to serve our armed forces - with the hope of one day, perhaps, returning to their home province.
Old friends are always welcome here!
Find a new home, yes - elsewhere.
Yang Sen Requests Support
Dire news has arrived from Chengdu wired through our Chief Officer in the Southwest, He Guoguang. The tenuous peace in the province of Sichuan has fallen apart as a direct result of the loss of stability of the Zhili National Order, following the troubles in the League of Eight Provinces. Greatly diminishing the influence of the Sichuanese leader, and key ally of the Zhili, Yang Sen, the internal divisions in the province have escalated into open conflict. Fellow Accelerated Department member and Chongqing warlord Liu Xiang, has turned on governor Yang sen and his forces with the largest army in the province in tow. For now at least, Yang's allies in the Baoding department under Deng Xihou, Liu Wenhui, and Tian Songyao remain, but even that is an uncertainty as the situation spirals further out of control with every passing day.\n\nAlready the Zhili Clique, frequently meeting behind closed doors, have begun to scramble for a response. With chaos seizing the administration, many have had to rely upon personality, rather than constitutionalism, to push through with their proposals. Albeit, despite all pretences, it is not a factional divide on the Sichuan Issue, but that of a logistical one.\n\nWith the current chaos in Sichuan, it cannot be ruled out that a prolonged conflict where both sides exhaust their strength could lead to the remnants of Xiong Kewu seizing the moment to reverse their old misfortunes. As if that wasn't enough, persistent droughts have hit Sichuan's already struggling people. With disaster looming, the Zhili's old friend, Governor Yang, has reached out to the Clique through He, pleading that it offers any support it may muster. While the consequences of a defeat for Yang could prove severe for the Clique in the future, neither the Jade Marshal nor King of Baoding have deigned to comment much, albeit in private it has been reported that Wu Peifu has prepared a small aid package for his old friend.
Send them what we can spare.
We can't spare anything right now.

The Zhili Abandons Us
It would appear nowadays that everyone within the nation has been cast away with misfortune. Betrayed by Liu Xiang already, and only tentatively holding an alliance with the Armament, Baoding, and Officer Departments, Governor Yang's desperate situation resulted in a casting of a lifeline towards Luoyang, or even Beijing. Through the Zhili's contact in the Southwest, He Guoguang, Yang was able to utilise his direct connection to his old friend Wu Peifu to enlist some form of support for his campaign against Liu.\n\nAnd yet, it would appear that the Central Government has deemed it unnecessary, or perhaps, is too busy, to aid the Governor in maintaining order. Far more concerned with internal matters following Nanjing's instability, rather than personal loyalty, the Zhili has refused to aid Yang, leaving the Governor to his own fate. With morale already plummeting, few of the common soldiery have hope that they will be able to defy Liu's army in men, or materiel.
Well, at least there are no allies left to betray us...
