Deng Hanxiang
§YBorn:§! §L1888, in Pan County, Guizhou Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §aAccelerated Department§! - §aFucheng Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAttending private schools throughout his childhood, Deng Hanxiang would be admitted to Kunming Normal School in 1905, later entering the Kunming Military Academy and Guizhou Army School. In 1909, he would study at the Hubei Army School, organising the Yunnan-Guizhou Association and serving as its president. During the Wuchang Uprising, Deng served as a captain of a student battalion, and subsequently served in other early revolutionary roles.\n\nFollowing Xinhai, Deng became a liaison between Yuan Shikai and Li Yuanhong, and in 1913 up until 1916, worked with Cai E to oppose Yuan's monarchy restoration. Becoming the Beijing representative to Tang Jiyao, consultant to the State Council and the Ministry of War, Deng floated between Yunnan, Guizhou, Zhejiang, and Sichuan in various military-diplomatic roles.\n\nIn 1922, Deng served as a representative of Duan Qirui to Sun Yat-sen, offering an alliance to take down the Zhili Clique. In 1924, he became Chief Counselor of the Zhejiang-Shanghai Allied Forces, and aided in the formation of Duan Qirui's 1925 cabinet. In 1926, Deng followed Duan to Tianjin, and in 1928 returned to Guizhou, before becoming Liu Xiang's representative to Beijing. Since 1935, Deng has been one of Liu's most trusted advisors, and a man that Liu consults before every important decision.§!
Qiao Yifu
§YBorn:§! §L1885, in Mianzhu County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §aAccelerated Department§! - §aFucheng Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from the Sichuan Military Academy and Sichuan Accelerated School in 1909, Qiao Yifu became an instructor at the Kunming Military Academy, and joined the Tongmenghui that year. After Xinhai, Qiao returned to Sichuan and served as a battalion commander under Liu Yuehou. In 1916, he fought in the National Protection War.\n\nIn 1919 he served as the representative of the Sichuan Army under Liu Xiang to Yunnan Province, and in 1921 became commander-in-chief of the Sichuan Army and special representative of the Sichuan Governor to Hankou. In 1927, Qiao became director of the Chongqing Municipal Police Department. And as of 1936, has recently become a senior staff officer in the Sichuan-Xikang Pacification Office.§!

At 13, he would travel to Chengdu, and settle there. In 1907, Meng entered Sichuan Higher School alongside the likes of Zeng Qi and Guo Moruo. In 1911, Meng entered the Cungu School (later to become the Sichuan National Academy), and was tutored intensely in the classics.\n\nAfter graduation in 1916, Meng would travel to Chengdu to teach Chinese at the Provincial United chinese School in 1919, and in 1921 moved to Chongqing for the same job. Wang Enyang
§YBorn:§! §L1897, in Nanchong County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LApolitical§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA disciple of Ouyang Jingwu, Wang Enyang would start his academic career at Nanchong Middle School, before moving to Beijing in 1919 to audit classes in the Department of Philosophy at Beijing University. Appreciated by Liang Shuming, he would be tutored under him. In 1923, Wang travelled to the China Inner Academy in Nanjing, established by Ouyang Jingwu, to study Buddhist scriptures, and participated intensely in the Buddhist philosophical debates engulfing China at the time.\n\nIn 1925, Enyang became the Director and Professor of the Inner Academy's Special Course, and in 1927 returned to Sichuan following the suspension of classes at the Academy due to the Northern Expedition. Establishing the Guishan Study Room in Nanchong, he would continue to teach Buddhism and Confucianism to students, and in 1930 was invited to the Chengdu Buddhist Society. As of now, Enyang has focused his efforts intensely upon teaching and writing, producing a variety of texts on Buddhism.§!
Wen Shaohe
§YBorn:§! §L1888, in Ba County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LApolitical§!\n§YBackground:§! §LThe Hui son of a prestigous county family, Wen Shaohe had a standard youth of progressively advancing education, which would then spurn on a long career in teaching. Becoming principal of Ba County Middle School, he would later teach at East Sichuan Normal School, and from 1914 to 1921 was inspector of the Ba County Education Promotion Office, later becoming Director of the Ba County Education Bureau. In 1922, Wen was sent as a representative of the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce to the All-China Chamber of Commerce conference in Shanghai, meeting various renowned figures such as Liang Qichao, Zhang Taiyan, and Huang Yanpei.\n\nIn 1923 he became director of the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce, and chairman of the Silk Industry Association. In 1928, Wen was re-elected to the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce, effectively establishing his own dominance for innumerable consecutive terms. That same year, Wen served on the Chongqing University preparatory committee, and in 1932 established his own Middle School, and expanded his education institutions to include three schools by 1935.§!\n\n§YNotes: Considered to be popular, diligent, and spartan, Wen Shaohe is well-liked amongst Sichuan's Hui, Commercial, and Warlord communities, and is one of Sichuan's most favourable local figures.§!

The next year, Li organised and presided over the work of the Chengdu branch of the Young China Association, editing its weekly magazine, and left for France the same year to study. Zeng Junchen
§YBorn:§! §LSeptember 6th 1888, in Weiyuan County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LApolitical§!\n§YBackground:§! §LApprenticing at a saltworks at a young age in Luzhou, Zeng Junchen would resign from his job in 1912, and begin a grain store. In 1914, he opened a restaurant, the largest in Luzhou, and in 1920 partnered with Hu Shaozhang and others to establish a salt company in Chongqing. In 1922, Zeng founded a hydropower plant, and in 1924 became the president of the Chongqing Salt Lobby. Cultivating close ties with bureaucrats and warlords, Zeng's salt business would amass him a fortune by 1928.\n\nAt the same time, Zeng co-founded the Shuyi Tobacco Factory with Shui Xiheng, albeit due to the influence of Wang Zunxu, Zeng's salt business would become bankrupt, and he would subsequently serve as manager of Pan Changyou's own salt transportation business. Ren Hongjun
§YBorn:§! §LDecember 20th, 1886, in Dianjiang, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LApolitical§!\n§YBackground:§! §LOne of China's most preeminent scholars, Ren Hongjun started his academic life being admitted to Dianjiang Academy in 1898. Intelligent, diligent, and amongst the best of the student body, Ren would take the final imperial examination in China, and in 1908 would travel to Japan to study applied chemistry. In 1909, he joined the Tongmenghui through the introduction of Dan Maoxin, and served as President of the Sichuan branch of the Tongmenghui.\n\nWriting revolutionary manifesto lambasting the Qing, Ren would oversea the sponsorship of revolutionaries to study in Tokyo, amongst them Chiang Kai-shek and Zhang Qun. After Xinhai, Ren was secretary to Sun Yat-sen, but would resign and travel to the USA to earn a master's degree in chemistry from Columbia University. Returning in 1918, Ren served as Director of the Education Department of the Ministry of Education, Professor of Beijing University, Editor of the Commercial Press in Shanghai, and Vice-President of the National Southeast University.\n\nIn 1935, Ren became president of Sichuan University, beginning an ambitious programme of multifaceted reform of its internal affairs. With his career at its highest, the most pressing thing on his mind is China's, and Sichuan's, lack of internal stability.§!
Jiang Kui
§YBorn:§! §L1893, in Ba County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LApolitical§!\n§YBackground:§! §LStudying at Chongqing Guangyi Academy, Jiang Kui would proceed onto the Shanghai Nanyang Middle School, before beginning his naval career at the Wusong Merchant Marine College. In 1914, joining the navy as a trainee, Jiang would transition towards the Third Avenue of warfare in 1915 after enrolling at Beijing Aviation School. Albeit after graduating, Jiang proceeded to return to the navy, and rise to the rank of first lieutenant.\n\nIn 1920, he travelled to Britain and the United States to study aircraft manufacturing and flight technology, then returning to China in 1922 to serve as a flight instructor and director of education at the Beijing Aviation Training Institute. Leading the air force in the Jiangsu-Zhejiang and ZhiFeng Wars, Jiang would be promoted to deputy commander of the Third Army's Air Force, before being transferred to the Aviation Bureau in 1925.\n\nConsidering defection during the Northern Expedition, Jiang would remain with Beiyang, and in 1928 visit France and Germany to study their air fleets. Returning to serve once more as an aviation instructor, Jiang would be hired by Liu Xiang in 1930 to aid in establishing an air force and navy in Sichuan. In 1935, Jiang resigned to serve as a professor at Chongqing University, however he has been kept on retainer, for any Sichuan Warlord that may need his services.§!
